Rice v. State


S06A1109.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


281 Ga. 149; 635 S.E.2d 707; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 600; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 3023



October 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied October 30, 2006.
Subsequent appeal at Rice v. State, 2012 Ga. LEXIS 853 (Ga., Oct. 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Staley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the murders of two victims and with related crimes. The State then gave notice of its intent to seek the death penalty. However, defendant was granted an interim review of the proceedings up to that point. The parties were thus directed to address issues pertaining to the same.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the trial court erred in (1) denying defendant's motion concerning the composition of the grand and traverse jury lists; (2) ruling that the pretrial deposition testimony of the husband of the female victim was admissible at trial; and (3) refusing to allow a second pretrial deposition of the victims' next door neighbor. The instant court found no error. First, defendant's own expert testimony showed that there was no under-representation of Hispanic citizens on the grand and traverse jury lists. Second, although defendant's opportunity for cross-examination was perhaps not ideal given the fact that he had only six days' notice of the hearing, he was afforded a sufficient opportunity to cross-examine a witness who later died, and the lack of cross-examination was the result of him waiving that opportunity. Thus, the witness's deposition was admissible at trial. Finally, because defendant had already questioned the next-door neighbor about the medications she was taking and whether in her subjective judgment her memory was affected by her medications, no abuse of discretion resulted in refusing defendant's request for any additional cross-examination.


OUTCOME: Finding no error in the proceedings thus far, the judgment was affirmed.

Walker v. State


S06P0992.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


281 Ga. 157; 635 S.E.2d 740; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 652; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 3029



October 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied October 30, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Walker v. Georgia, 552 U.S. 833, 128 S. Ct. 60, 169 L. Ed. 2d 50, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9247 (2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Chatman v. Walker, 2015 Ga. LEXIS 360 (Ga., June 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Camden Superior Court. Before Judge Wilkes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of malice murder, possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. A kidnapping charge was dismissed by order of nolle prosequi. The trial court (Georgia) imposed a death sentence for the murder and five-year sentences for the firearm charges. Defendant's motion for new trial was denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence did not support the conviction. The state's highest court held that the evidence supported the conviction. Any error in notifying defendant of the statutory aggravating circumstances was harmless. Challenges to the discretion of district attorneys to decide whether to pursue the death penalty had been rejected. O.C.G.A. § 17-10-30(b)(7) was not unconstitutional. Qualifying prospective jurors based upon their death penalty views did not violate defendant's right to an impartial jury. Nine prospective jurors were properly excused. Defendant was not entitled to a new trial on the possession of a firearm by a convicted felon charge. The trial on the possession of a firearm charge did not impermissibly place defendant's character in issue at sentencing. The evidence supported the possession of a firearm by a convicted felon conviction. The jury was properly instructed at sentencing. The kidnapping offense was properly the basis of an aggravating circumstance. The death sentence was not imposed under any arbitrary factor and the statutory aggravating circumstances were supported by the evidence. Finally, the death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Baker v. State


S06A0500.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 822; 633 S.E.2d 541; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 489; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 2371



July 18, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 16-5-60 (b); constitutional question. Lowndes State Court. Before Judge Turner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the trial court (Georgia) of misdemeanor reckless conduct in violation of O.C.G.A. § 16-5-60(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 16-5-60(b) was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court held that the evidence supported the conviction. Defendant left his nine-month-old and three-year-old sons unsupervised on the upper floor of a two-story home near an unprotected downward flight of stairs, which was a gross deviation from the standard of care that a reasonable person would exercise and was in conscious disregard of a substantial and unjustifiable risk such that his act endangered the children's safety. Section 16-5-60(b) was not unconstitutionally vague. The statute gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice that it prohibited a person from leaving one's children, one an infant and the other a toddler, unsupervised on the upper floor of a two-story home that was not equipped with any device to keep the children from falling down a nearby flight of stairs. Finally, defendant's theory that he had no legal duty to the children, despite being their father, since he did not live with them was rejected. There was no harmful error in the officer's recitation of the factors that led him or her to initiate the reckless conduct charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

245 of 777 DOCUMENTS




Perdue v. O'Kelley


S06A1574.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 732; 632 S.E.2d 110; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 465; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 2181



July 6, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proposed constitutional amendment; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Russell.
O'Kelley v. Cox, 278 Ga. 572, 604 S.E.2d 773, 2004 Ga. LEXIS 953 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed an action against defendant, seeking a declaration that Ga. Const. art. I, § IV, para. I was unconstitutional. The trial court (Georgia) found the section unconstitutional. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the first sentence of Ga. Const. art. I, § IV, para. I(b) dealt with how same-sex relationships were treated, was a different subject than defining marriage as the union of man and woman, and so, the section violated the multiple subject matter rule, Ga. Const. art. X, § I, para. II. The appellate court found that the objective of Ga. Const. art. I, § IV, para. I was the non-recognition of same sex conjugal relationships and to define marriage exclusively as the union between man and woman. The commonality of those expressions was exclusiveness, establishing that marriage and its attendant benefits belonged only to unions of man and woman. That exclusiveness was the essence of the amendment's purpose. The prohibition against recognizing same-sex unions as entitled to the benefits of marriage was not "dissimilar and discordant" to the objective of reserving the status of marriage and its attendant benefits exclusively to unions of man and woman. Ga. Const. art. I, § IV, para. I(b) did not address a different objective than that of the amendment as a whole and did not render the amendment violative of the multiple-subject matter rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Moseley v. Sentence Review Panel


S06A0035.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 646; 631 S.E.2d 704; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 444; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1954



June 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Sentence Review Panel v. Moseley, 284 Ga. 128, 663 S.E.2d 679, 2008 Ga. LEXIS 567 (Ga., July 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sentencing; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wyatt Cummings Moore.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant district attorney brought an action against appellee sentencing panel, its members, and other officials, seeking mandamus and injunctive relief relating to the sentencing panel's reduction of the sentence of a criminal defendant. The trial court (Georgia) granted the sentencing panel's motion to dismiss. The district attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: Notwithstanding a plea bargain in the underlying case pursuant to which the criminal defendant agreed to a 15-year sentence, the panel reduced her sentence to 8 years. The trial court found that the district attorney lacked standing to bring his case because he was only authorized to recommend a sentence to be imposed at the discretion of the trial court and, thus, has no interest at stake when the panel reduced a sentence. The appellate court held that, because the district attorney's complaint did not seek enforcement of the panel's performance of its public duties, but challenged the validity of the duties that the general assembly authorized it to exercise, he lacked standing to attack the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 17-10-6 by means of mandamus. However, the complaint also sought an injunction against enforcement of § 17-10-6, which he alleged was unconstitutional. Among the district attorney's official responsibilities was the obligation to challenge, on constitutional grounds, a statute which allegedly interfered with his authority as a judicial officer to negotiate binding plea agreements in criminal cases. Thus he had standing to seek an injunction.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding that the district attorney lacked standing to seek a writ of mandamus was affirmed. The judgment holding that the district attorney lacked standing to seek an injunction was reversed and the case was remanded for consideration of the constitutional issue.

 

247 of 777 DOCUMENTS




Coffey v. Fayette County


S06A0055.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 656; 631 S.E.2d 703; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 448; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1937



June 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Coffey v. Fayette County, 289 Ga. App. 153, 656 S.E.2d 262, 2008 Ga. App. LEXIS 23 (Ga. Ct. App., Jan. 9, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equity. Fayette Superior Court. Before Judge English.
Coffey v. Fayette County, 279 Ga. 111, 610 S.E.2d 41, 2005 Ga. LEXIS 165 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents brought an action against defendant county, challenging the constitutionality of a sign ordinance adopted by the county. Following an earlier appeal, reversal, and remand, the trial court (Georgia) held that certain provisions in the ordinance were unconstitutional, but severed those provisions and upheld the redacted statute. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: In reaching its conclusion, the trial court received no evidence from the county but nonetheless held that if, in the county's estimation, only one sign and only one size adequately promoted traffic safety, the trial court was not in a position to dispute this conclusion. The trial court also held that if in the county's estimation limiting the number and size of signs in residential areas was the only way to maintain the aesthetic goals it wished to maintain, the trial court would not question its conclusion. The appellate court held that, in considering the constitutionality of ordinances restricting free speech, the courts were required to review the ordinance closely to ensure that it was narrowly drawn to serve the governmental interest. In conducting this close review, a court was not permitted to merely defer to the discretion of the governmental entity imposing the ordinance. In this case, the trial court improperly deferred without question to the decisions made at the discretion of the county without receiving any evidence or fully considering whether the ordinance was the least restrictive means of achieving the county's goals.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to fully consider whether the ordinance was narrowly tailored and the least restrictive means to achieve the county's goals.


 

248 of 777 DOCUMENTS




R.J. Taylor Mem. Hosp., Inc. v. Beck


S06A0402, S06X0403.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 660; 631 S.E.2d 684; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 451; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1935



June 26, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Forum non conveniens; motion to transfer venue. Bibb State Court. Before Judge Adams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sued defendant hospital, and others, alleging medical malpractice. The hospital moved to transfer venue to a different county. The State Court of Bibb County (Georgia) held, inter alia, that O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31(c) was unconstitutional, declined to transfer case pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31.1(a), and denied the motion. The hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hospital argued that the O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31.1(a) factors of forum non conveniens supported transferring the case to Pulaski County in that, inter alia, the patient was a resident of Pulaski County, the hospital was in Pulaski County, the patient's medical records were in Pulaski County, and all interactions between the patient and the several defendants occurred in Pulaski County. The appellate court disagreed. Initially, the trial court properly ruled that O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31(c) was unconstitutional. The hospital failed to meet its burden of showing an abuse of the trial court's discretion in the denial of the motion to transfer. There was no showing that litigating the matter in Bibb County, where several of the defendants resided, posed difficulties with regard to interviewing or securing witnesses and evidence or that relocating the case to Pulaski County would allow easier access. Further, since Bibb and Pulaski Counties were not at great distance from one another, it was difficult to accept the assertions that what was at issue affected the receipt of medical care solely in Pulaski County or that there was no local interest in deciding the case in Bibb County.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

249 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Widner v. State


S06A0443, S06A1547.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 675; 631 S.E.2d 675; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 459; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1961



June 26, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA §§ 16-6-4 (d) (1), 17-10-6.1; constitutional question. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge McGarity.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the trial court (Georgia) convicted defendant of two counts of aggravated child molestation and one count of statutory rape. The trial court imposed a mandatory sentence for aggravated child molestation of 10 years without parole pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 16-6-4(d)(1) and O.C.G.A. § 17-10-6.1. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his mandatory sentence for aggravated child molestation of 10 years without parole was cruel and unusual punishment as applied to him. Defendant contended that his crime should have been given special treatment and excepted from the mandated punishment because he was 18 at the time of the act and the victim was only 4 years younger. The appellate court found, however, that the law at the time of the commission of the crime provided no such exception, and, because the required punishment did not unconstitutionally shock the conscience, defendant's sentence stood. Defendant, a legal adult, pursued the victim and got her to agree to have sex with him and another male friend at the same time, despite the fact that the victim's parents previously told him that she was only 14 years old. Based on these facts and applying the requisite deference to the legislative branch's authority to impose punishment based on the mores of society at the time of the crime, defendant's sentence was appropriate under O.C.G.A. § 16-6-4(d)(1) and was not so disproportionate as to shock the conscience.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stanfield v. Glynn County


S06A0452, S06X0453.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 785; 631 S.E.2d 374; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 388; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1825



June 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied July 14, 2006.
Related proceeding at Stanfield v. Waste Mgmt. of Ga., Inc., 287 Ga. App. 810, 652 S.E.2d 815, 2007 Ga. App. LEXIS 1041 (Ga. Ct. App., Sept. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Tuten.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in Case Numbers S06A0452 and S06X0453.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents sued, among others, defendant county and corporation, asserting nuisance, trespass, and inverse condemnation arising from the corporation's waste transfer facility adjacent to property on which the residents resided. The trial court (Georgia) granted summary judgment for the county, and denied summary judgment motions filed by the corporation and the residents. The corporation and the residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the county's actions did not rise to an inverse condemnation, which was necessary for recovery of damages. The appellate court agreed. The residents were allowed to recover if and only if the trespass or nuisance amounted to the taking of property without just compensation. The county's approval of the construction of the waste transfer facility and its issuance of building permits did not subject it to liability for inverse condemnation or for any claim rising to that level. The issuance of citations for violation of the nuisance ordinance did not show that the county was responsible for maintaining a nuisance. The trial court also correctly held that a waste transfer facility was a permissible use in the general industrial district. There was at least some evidence presented in opposition to the corporation's summary judgment motion which showed that its facility generated odor, noise, dust, and various pests, and that these conditions resulted in disturbance, discomfort, and annoyance to the residents and a diminution in the value of their home. Glynn County, Ga., Ordinance § 2-16-237 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.


 

251 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Hinton v. State


S06A0459.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 811; 631 S.E.2d 365; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 390; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1853



June 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied July 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Workman.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder in the Georgia trial court and was sentenced to life in prison. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim's body was never found. The evidence established that she and defendant had left a ball park where they worked within five minutes of each other, that her car was found at a gas station near the park, that a person whose voice characteristics matched defendant's said on the phone he had taken the victim at "the station," and that the park and the gas station were in DeKalb County. The high court held that as this evidence was sufficient to prove that the murder might have been committed in DeKalb County, the proper trial venue under O.C.G.A. § 17-2-2(h) was proved to be in that county. The evidence, including defendant's incriminating statements to fellow inmates, was sufficient to convict. Evidence of defendant's attempted rape of one woman and his kidnapping and sexual molestation of another, which occurred 17 and 12 years earlier, respectively, was properly admitted to show plan and scheme, motive, intent and frame of mind, including lustful disposition; the time interval was acceptable. O.C.G.A. § 24-9-84.1(b), which barred defendant from impeaching State witnesses by their convictions that were over 10 years old, did not violate the Confrontation Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

252 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Fulton County v. Perdue


S06A0449.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 807; 631 S.E.2d 362; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 399; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1819



June 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied July 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: OCGA § 36-31-12; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Goger.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county filed a declaratory judgment action, arguing that O.C.G.A. § 36-31-12, which governed a county's collection of revenue and distribution of government services within special tax districts, was both unconstitutional and inapplicable to the county. Appellees, the State and Governor of Georgia, filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-11-12(c), which the Georgia trial court granted. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the power granted to it by a local constitutional amendment, 1972 Ga. Laws 1482, § 1, the county created a special taxing and spending district (SSD) that included all of its unincorporated areas, including noncontiguous areas separated by incorporated municipalities. It collected taxes and fees to pay for services provided exclusively within its SSD, but did not limit the expenditure of this revenue to the area in which it was collected. After the incorporation of a city within its borders, it filed the instant action. It argued that § 36-31-12(b) was inapplicable to its existing SSD because § 36-31-12(b) applied only when noncontiguous areas were first created by the incorporation of a new municipality. The trial court held that § 36-31-12(b) did not apply only to SSDs with newly created noncontiguous areas, and appellate court concurred. Section § 36-31-12(b) did not violate the Georgia Constitution by encroaching on the county's exclusive authority, derived from 1972 Ga. Laws 1482, § 1, over the collection and expenditure of revenues collected within its SSD; 1972 Ga. Laws 1482, § 1 granted concurrent authority to the county and legislature over this matter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

253 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Harbuck v. State


S06A0137.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 775; 631 S.E.2d 351; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 401; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1842



June 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied July 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: OCGA § 40-6-395 (a); constitutional question. Douglas State Court. Before Judge Dettmering.
Harbuck v. State, 2004 Ga. LEXIS 124 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in a Georgia trial court convicted defendant of violating O.C.G.A. § 40-6-395(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged her conviction. However, none of her claims warranted reversal. First, her failure to yield to uniformed police officer driving a marked police vehicle supported the conviction, and whether her failure to stop was wilful was a question for the jury upon consideration of the words, conduct, demeanor, motive, and all other circumstances connected with the act. Second, inasmuch as her motion to quash the accusation contested the authenticity of the State's evidence and did not attack the accusation for a facial defect, denial of the motion was not erroneous. Third, the pursuing officer was not called upon to exercise the legislative function of defining what constituted a crime, but the executive branch function of enforcing the law. Fourth, there was no constitutional requirement that a criminal statute had to contain a statement that a justification defense be asserted. Fifth, denial of a motion in arrest of judgment was not error, as the State Court of Douglas County had subject-matter jurisdiction over the case. Finally, since defendant was not found guilty of a wilful failure to stop, her contention that she could not be tried for the same was moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

254 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Couch v. Parker


S06A0229. S06A0261.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 580; 630 S.E.2d 364; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 239; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1336



April 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied June 12, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: OCGA § 12-2-2 (c) (3) (B); constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Tusan.
Parker v. Scrap Metal Processors, Inc., 386 F.3d 993, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 20381 (11th Cir. Ga., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Georgia superior court reversed a ruling by an administrative law judge (ALJ), finding that appellee homeowners were aggrieved or adversely affected by the consent orders entered by appellant, the Director of the Environmental Protection Division of the Department of Natural Resources (Director), and that O.C.G.A. § 12-2-2(c)(3)(B) could not unconstitutionally bar the homeowners' pursuit of an appeal. The Director and the company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Director and the company challenged the finding that O.C.G.A. § 12-2-2(c)(3)(B) was unconstitutional as applied to the homeowners. The instant court first held that the homeowners did not have a constitutional due process right to pursue any claim which was paramount to the legislature's constitutional authority to create, modify, or abolish the right to sue. Second, § 12-2-2(c)(3)(B) did not bar the homeowners from seeking redress in the courts for the injury they allegedly sustained but was a legislative limitation on standing to appeal an order rendered by the Director. But, the flaw in the homeowners' claims was that the intent underlying § 12-2-2(c)(3)(B) was to preclude attacks on the Director's determination of the scope of remedial measures set forth in consent orders issued under the Hazardous Site Response Act. Until they obtain a full satisfaction, the homeowners could pursue all available legal remedies against those responsible for polluting their property. However, insofar as administrative remedies were concerned, the homeowners did not have standing to appeal the Director's consent orders unless and until she sought to enforce them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

255 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Fielden


S06A0282. S06A0283.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 444; 629 S.E.2d 252; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 247; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1351



April 25, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 16-11-34 (a); constitutional question. Lowndes State Court. Before Judge Turner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with violating O.C.G.A. § 16-11-34(a). The trial court (Georgia) dismissed the case. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that O.C.G.A. § 16-11-34(a) was unconstitutionally vague. However, the appellate court found that § 16-11-34 provided a sufficiently definite warning to a person of ordinary intelligence of the prohibited conduct, namely, the reckless or knowing commission of any act which may reasonably have been expected to disrupt or prevent a lawful meeting, gathering, or process, and further that it was not susceptible to arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The appellate court agreed with the trial court, however, that § 16-11-34(a) was overbroad. Under the literal language of the statute, the only proof required was that the person recklessly or knowingly committed any act that may reasonably have been expected to prevent or disrupt a lawful meeting, gathering or procession. It did not matter where or when the accused committed the proscribed act, or even whether the act, upon its commission, resulted in any actual prevention or disruption. The literal language of the statute was so overbroad in its scope that it led to an absurdity manifestly not intended by the legislature, and its constitutionality could not have been preserved by judicial construction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

256 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Findley v. Findley


S06A0424.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 454; 629 S.E.2d 222; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 254; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 1337



April 25, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Domestic relations. Evans Superior Court. Before Judge Jackson from Waycross Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Georgia trial court denied petitioner wife's application for contempt, ruling that the estate of respondent, her late ex-husband, was not obligated to make monthly alimony payments to her because said obligation did not survive his death. The court also directed the wife to pay $ 500 attorney fees to the estate. The wife sought further review, which was granted, and this matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The incorporated agreement at issue expressly provided that the ex-husband's obligation to pay the car and furniture debts, and the wife's right to live in the marital home he owned, expressly survived his death, but no such express provision was made regarding the payment of periodic alimony. But, after deciding not to depart from the general rule of retroactivity of judicial decisions, since the provision entitling the wife to alimony until she remarried or died did not evidence a manifest intention to reverse the normal rule that the death of the obligor terminated the obligation to pay alimony, and the settlement agreement lacked a clear expression of intent to extend alimony payments beyond the death of the ex-husband, the trial court properly denied the wife's motion to hold the estate responsible for the alimony obligation. Second, if the award of attorney fees to the estate was predicated on O.C.G.A. § 9-15-14(b), it was erroneous, as the findings necessary to support such an award were not made. Further, if attorney's fee were based on O.C.G.A. § 19-6-2, it was also erroneous, as there was no evidence of the parties' financial circumstances that authorized such an award.


OUTCOME: Denial of the wife's application for contempt was affirmed. But, the award of attorney's fees was reversed.

Fulton County v. City of Atlanta


S06A0049.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 353; 629 S.E.2d 196; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 199; 62 ERC (BNA) 1735; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 951



March 27, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Interstate commerce; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county sued defendant city, seeking declaratory and equitable relief pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 36-1-16(a). The trial court (Georgia) entered summary judgment for the city. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dispute arose out of contracts whereby municipal solid waste was collected in the city, taken to transfer stations in the county, and transported to landfills for final disposal. The trial court found that O.C.G.A. § 36-1-16(a) was unconstitutional because it impaired interstate commerce. The appellate court agreed. O.C.G.A. § 36-1-16(a) gave Georgia counties the power to veto the importation of solid waste. This it was not permitted to do. A state, or one of its political subdivisions, was not allowed to avoid the strictures of the Commerce Clause by curtailing the movement of articles of commerce through subdivisions of the state, rather than through the state itself.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

258 of 777 DOCUMENTS



SEIU v. Perdue


S05A1634.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 379; 628 S.E.2d 589; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 206; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 954; 24 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 595; 152 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,175



March 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied April 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: State Merit System; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Tusan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs state employees and their union filed suit in which they challenged the constitutionality of the 1996 and 2000 amendments to O.C.G.A. § 45-20-2(15). The trial court (Georgia) found that the amendments did not violate Ga. Const. art. IV, § III, para. I(b). The state employees and the union appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state employees and the union alleged that the amendments to O.C.G.A. § 45-20-2(15) violated Ga. Const. art. IV, § III, para. I(b), and specifically contended that Ga. Const. art. IV, § III, para. I(b) mandated a state merit system which was required to include such traditional features as tenure and appeal rights. The appellate court disagreed. Ga. Const. art. IV, § III, para. I did not mention tenure and the right to appeal. That constitutional provision did not create the state merit system. Instead, it only created a state personnel board, and then provided in Ga. Const. art. IV, § III, para. I(b) that that board was to provide policy direction for a state merit system of personnel administration and may have been vested with such additional powers and duties as provided by law. State personnel were to be selected on the basis of merit as provided by law. Ga. Const. art. IV, § III, para. I left it to the general assembly to actually create the state merit system by enactment of laws regarding the selection of state personnel based upon merit. Legislation providing systems for public employment was subject to amendment or even repeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

259 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Sherrod v. State


S05A1952.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 275; 627 S.E.2d 36; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 145; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 590



February 27, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 16-8-4 (c) (2); constitutional question. Bulloch Superior Court. Before Judge Martin, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with theft by conversion of leased property. Defendant moved the trial court (Georgia) to declare O.C.G.A. § 16-8-4(c)(2) unconstitutional. The motion was denied. Defendant was tried by the court, found guilty, and sentenced. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendant leased a stereo and failed to either pay for or return it. Defendant argued that O.C.G.A. § 16-8-4(c)(2) contained an unconstitutional mandatory presumption. The appellate court agreed. The statutory presumption in § 16-8-4(c)(2) was mandatory; if the State proved that the demand letter was sent in accordance with the statute, the defendant "shall be presumed" to have committed the elements of the crime. The State's presentation of its case relied on the statutory presumption. The trial court pronounced defendant guilty immediately after restating its ruling that the mandatory presumption was constitutional, and the trial court thus considered itself bound by the mandatory language in § 16-8-4(c)(2). The mandatory presumption applied to both the fact of conversion and defendant's intent, and the evidence was not overwhelming. Thus, the error was not harmless. However, defendant failed in her assertion that, without the operation of the presumption, the State presented insufficient evidence to sustain a conviction, and thus, retrial of defendant was allowed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

260 of 777 DOCUMENTS



EHCA Cartersville, LLC v. Turner


S05A1560, S05A2066.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 333; 626 S.E.2d 482; 2006 Ga. LEXIS 114; 2006 Fulton County D. Rep. 440



February 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied March 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Venue; constitutional question. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge DelCampo.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S05A1560. Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part in Case No. S05A2066.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate cases, one alleging medical malpractice, a Georgia trial court held that O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31(c) was unconstitutional, as applied in the first action, but that § 9-10-31(c) was not unconstitutional as applied in the second. Both defendants and plaintiff appealed, and the court granted a consolidated review of both judgments. The second action also involved the interpretation of O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31.1.


OVERVIEW: On an appeal from the first action, defendants argued that O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31(c) was authorized by Ga. Const. art. VI, § II, para. VIII. But, even if it was not, the statute did not violate the Constitution's joint tortfeasor provision. They further alleged that O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31(c) authorized a venue transfer from one county where venue was proper to another county where venue was proper. The instant court disagreed. Also § 9-10-31(c) was not a proper exercise of the legislature's authority to enact laws which allowed the superior and state courts to change venue. In the second case, one of the defendants moved to transfer venue pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31.1(a). The plaintiff alleged that the trial court erred, and defendants alleged that § 9-10-31.1(a) was authorized by Ga. Const. art. VI, § II, para. VIII, and thus did not conflict with Ga. Const. art. VI, § II, para. IV. The court held that because O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31.1(a) vested power to change venue in the court, and not in a defendant, as did O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31(c), O.C.G.A. § 9-10-31.1(a) was a proper under Ga. Const. art. VI, § II, para. VIII, and did not violate Ga. Const. art. VI, § II, para. IV.


OUTCOME: In the first action, the judgment was affirmed. In the second action, the constitutionality finding was reversed but retroactive application of the forum non conveniens statute was affirmed.

Nance v. State


S05P1438.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 125; 623 S.E.2d 470; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 855; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 3742



December 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied January 17, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nance v. Georgia, 127 S. Ct. 168, 166 L. Ed. 2d 119, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6966 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Clark.
Nance v. State, 274 Ga. 311, 553 S.E.2d 794, 2001 Ga. LEXIS 764 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from a Georgia trial court, which imposed the death sentence after the previously imposed death sentence was reversed and the matter was remanded for resentencing. Defendant had been convicted of malice murder, felony murder, aggravated assault, theft by taking, criminal attempt to commit armed robbery, and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole a car, drove to a bank, and robbed the teller at gunpoint. Defendant then fatally shot a driver while attempting to escape in his car. After shooting at another individual, defendant eventually surrendered. He was convicted and sentenced to death for the malice murder. Imposition of a death sentence on the felony murder conviction, which had been previously vacated, was error. The sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court with respect to imposition of the death sentence. The court vacated the sentence imposed on the conviction for felony murder.

Marks v. State


S05A1729.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 70; 623 S.E.2d 504; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 861; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 3746



December 1, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA §§ 15-19-51, 30-5-8; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Coursey.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from a Georgia trial court, which convicted him of multiple offenses, including unlawful abuse, neglect, or exploitation of elder persons and unauthorized practice of law, in violation of O.C.G.A. §§ 30-5-8(a)(1) and 15-19-51(a)(7), respectively. Defendant's challenges to the constitutionality of those statutes were found to lack merit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant financially exploited an 89-year-old widower by befriending him, acting as a lawyer, and obtaining his property and forging or coercing signatures on estate documents. He was indicted and he sought dismissal of the indictment, claiming that O.C.G.A. § 30-5-8(a)(1) was vague and violated equal protection, and that O.C.G.A. § 15-19-51(a)(7) violated the First Amendment. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the statutes, and defendant was convicted. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions. V, as he had no right to deceive or mislead people regarding his false ability to practice law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

263 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Mayze


S05A1225.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


280 Ga. 5; 622 S.E.2d 836; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 825; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 3521



November 21, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 16-9-125; constitutional question. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Boswell.
State v. Mayze, 2005 Ga. LEXIS 638 (Ga., Oct. 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in Clayton County with two counts of identity fraud in violation of O.C.G.A. § 16-9-121. Defendant's demurrer to the indictment was sustained. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the venue provision of O.C.G.A. § 16-9-125 violated Ga. Const. art. art. VI, § II, para. VI, which required that the venue of a criminal case be set in the county where the crime was committed. The state's highest court held that the nature of identity fraud was the protection of the personal information contained in the victim's records. That information was deemed to be in the lawful possession of the victim, so that when a defendant violated O.C.G.A. § 16-9-121 by engaging in an unauthorized access to the records, he engaged in the fraudulent use of information located in the county where the victim resided or was found. Since the crime of identity fraud, as defined by O.C.G.A. §§ 16-9-121 and 16-9-125 when read in para materia, took place in the county where the victim and his or her personal information were located, there was no constitutional bar to trying the defendant in that county. O.C.G.A. § 16-9-125 complied with the constitutional mandate. As it was alleged that defendant committed the crime of identity fraud in Clayton County by using personal information that was in the lawful possession of a resident of that county, venue was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Tennille v. State


S05A0927.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 884; 622 S.E.2d 346; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 848; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 3509



November 21, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 16-12-100; constitutional question. Baker Superior Court. Before Judge Porter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from a Georgia trial court, which convicted him of sexual exploitation of children, in violation of O.C.G.A. § 16-12-100(b)(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendant consented to a search of his home, which produced photographs of nude young females from a folder on defendant's computer. Defendant was indicted on 21 counts of sexual exploitation of children. His motion to dismiss, based on the asserted unconstitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 16-12-100, was denied. A bench trial was held, at which an expert witness testified that the persons in the photographs were under the age of 18. Defendant was convicted of 12 counts. On appeal, defendant claimed that the exemptions in § 16-12-100(d) made the statute unconstitutional because there was no express exemption for the defense in a criminal prosecution. The court found that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute, as he could not show that the statute adversely impacted his rights because he had made no effort to obtain the materials seized from his home for the purpose of preparing for trial. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions, and the issue of whether equal access rebutted the inference of possession was within the province of the trier of fact.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

265 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Griffin v. City Council


S05A0780.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 835; 621 S.E.2d 734; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 761



November 7, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] City government; constitutional question. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge Towson, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mayor sued defendants, a city council and its members, in the superior court (Georgia) to prevent them from changing the city's form of government. The trial court found the office of mayor was not abolished in violation of O.C.G.A. § 1-3-11, local legislation passed by the general assembly to accomplish the change was not unconstitutional, and defendants were entitled to judgment as a matter of law. The mayor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city council voted unanimously to change the city's government from a strong mayor/weak council system to a weak mayor/strong council system with a city manager, and the legislature passed an enabling act. The supreme court held this act amending the city charter did not abolish the mayor's office. Transferring duties on which the political power of the mayor's office was based to the council or city manager did not violate O.C.G.A. § 1-3-11. Nothing in § 1-3-11 barred altering the mayor's duties as long as his remaining duties were appropriate to the office. No referendum was required under § 1-3-11 as the act did not abolish his office, nor was a public hearing required, under O.C.G.A. § 28-1-14. The act's lack of language on council votes needed to approve the mayor's committee recommendations did not make the act invalid, given the city charter. The mayor, who was African-American, showed no equal protection violation, nor did he rebut evidence that the council enacted a more efficient form of government. He showed no unconstitutional diminution in African-American voters' political power, as he did not show the act was a purposeful device to further racial discrimination.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

267 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Rochefort v. State


S05A1413.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 738; 620 S.E.2d 803; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 665; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 3146



October 11, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 16-13-30.3 (b) (1); constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Bodiford.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the trial court (Georgia) of possession of more than 300 tablets of ephedrine, possession of methamphetamine, and shoplifting and from his sentence, following the denial of his motion for a directed verdict of acquittal, in which he challenged the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 16-13-30.3(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 16-13-30.3(b)(1) was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that § 16-13-30.3(b)(1) was constitutional as it created classifications with a rational basis in combatting the illicit drug trade. Further, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. "Ephedrine," "pseudoephedrine," and "phenylpropanolamine" were so similar to one another that each was considered a functional equivalent of the others. The State's expert witness testified that ephedrine and pseudoephedrine had the exact same chemical formulas and had the same effect on a body. The evidence supported the convictions. The equal access rule did not apply as defendant also made inculpatory admissions. The random testing of only two of the 2,329 tablets did not require an acquittal as the expert testified that the rest of the tablets all had the same logo and appearance; she also opined that all of the tablets contained pseudoephedrine. There was not a fatal variance, even though the accusation charged defendant with possession of ephedrine, but the proof showed that the tablets contained pseudoephedrine. For purposes of § 16-13-30.3, "ephedrine" and "pseudoephedrine" were synonymous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

268 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Alexander v. State


S05A0929.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 683; 620 S.E.2d 792; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 633



October 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Alexander v. State, 276 Ga. App. 288, 623 S.E.2d 160, 2005 Ga. App. LEXIS 1232 (Ga. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] False imprisonment statute; constitutional question. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge Hankinson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of burglary and false imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, without permission, crawled through a window into the home where a relative of his was living. Defendant then entered her bedroom and, while she was sleeping, placed his hand over her mouth and pinned her to the bed, thereby restricting her movement. The relative woke up and screamed. Defendant fled. He later admitted that he had entered the relative's home. The relative and others positively identified him as the intruder. He was charged with burglary and false imprisonment. At his first trial, the State redacted the burglary count from the indictment and proceeded only on the count of false imprisonment. However, a mistrial occurred. At his retrial, the State tried him on both the burglary and false imprisonment counts. He was convicted on both counts. The trial court then denied his motion for a new trial. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the evidence sufficiently supported the convictions, retrial on the burglary charge did not violate his double jeopardy rights, Georgia's false imprisonment statute, O.C.G.A. § 16-5-41(a), was not unconstitutionally vague, defendant was properly sentenced, and no error occurred in denying his motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

269 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Hough v. State


S05G0311. S05G0640.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 711; 620 S.E.2d 380; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 647



October 3, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Case No. S05G0311. Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 269 Ga. App. 744, 605 S.E.2d 43.

Case No. S05G0640. Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 270 Ga. App. 676, 607 S.E.2d 899.
Handschuh v. State, 270 Ga. App. 676, 607 S.E.2d 899, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 1586 (2004)
Hough v. State, 269 Ga. App. 744, 605 S.E.2d 43, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 1189 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the first of two cases consolidated for appeal, the Court of Appeals (Georgia) found that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the results of a blood test following a traffic accident. In the second case, the Court of Appeals reversed the trial court and found that defendant's refusal to submit to a blood test following an accident should have been suppressed. The State and one defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, defendant argued that he was not properly placed under arrest before the reading of his implied consent rights. The appellate court found that before the reading of his implied consent rights, defendant was involved in a traffic accident resulting in serious injuries to himself and the investigating officer had probable cause to believe that defendant was driving under the influence. Under these circumstances, the investigating officer was not required to arrest defendant before the reading of implied consent rights, and defendant's consent to the blood test was valid. Because defendant in the second case was not involved in a traffic accident resulting in serious injuries or fatalities as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 40-5-55(a), his refusal should have been suppressed. None of the § 40-5-55(a) situations was present as defendant's paralysis was not listed as one of the maladies on the very specific list provided by the legislature. Accordingly, the rules associated with the reading of implied consent rights to a suspect following a traffic accident with serious injuries or fatalities did not apply, and the trial court erred by denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

270 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Lewis v. State


S05P0906.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 756; 620 S.E.2d 778; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 523; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 2838



September 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied October 24, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lewis v. Ga., 547 U.S. 1116, 126 S. Ct. 1917, 164 L. Ed. 2d 671, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3608 (U.S., May 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Douglas Superior Court. Before Judge James.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Georgia trial court sentencing him to death after convicting him, pursuant to his guilty plea, of malice murder, felony murder, feticide, aggravated battery, and kidnapping with bodily injury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he murdered the victim, who was eight or nine months pregnant. Defendant picked up the victim. After the victim stripped naked, defendant pinned her arms to the ground, choked her, and stabbed her in the throat and chest. Defendant also murdered three prostitutes. Where one prospective juror made a comment that defendant killed redheads and where that juror was later excused, the trial court did not err in refusing to excuse other prospective jurors. The parties individually questioned the relevant prospective jurors about the redheads remark and other conversation that the victim had been pregnant. The information that the victim had been pregnant and was murdered was to be presented at trial. Defendant's trial was not affected by pretrial publicity since all of the qualified jurors indicated that they could decide the case by only considering the evidence presented. Defendant was not entitled to have his death sentence vacated on mental illness grounds. O.C.G.A. § 17-7-131 did not preclude a death sentence on mental illness grounds. Also, there was no constitutional prohibition against a death sentence for a competent but mentally ill defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

271 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Perkins v. State


S05A0728.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 506; 614 S.E.2d 92; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 408; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 1772



June 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied June 30, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Perkins v. Ga., 546 U.S. 1033, 126 S. Ct. 748, 163 L. Ed. 2d 573, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8618 (U.S., Nov. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Double jeopardy; constitutional question. Whitfield Superior Court. Before Judge Morris.
State v. Perkins, 262 Ga. App. 62, 584 S.E.2d 680, 2003 Ga. App. LEXIS 840 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's conviction in the probate court for reckless driving was declared null and void, the Whitfield County Superior Court (Georgia) ruled that double jeopardy did not bar his retrial in that court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was cited for reckless driving in an automobile collision resulting in a death. He pled guilty in the probate court. He was subsequently indicted for felony vehicular homicide in the trial court arising from the same incident. On appeal, the probate court conviction was set aside as null and void under O.C.G.A. § 40-6-376(d). The supreme court held it had previously decided that when a court had no jurisdiction to try a defendant, any conviction entered by that court was null and void, but a defendant whose conviction was so voided could be retried without the attachment of procedural double jeopardy. As a result, defendant could be retried on the felony indictment in the trial court. Any substantive double jeopardy issues that might arise if defendant was convicted were not decided. Defendant's claim that § 40-6-376(d) was unconstitutional on its face was without merit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

272 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. State


S04G1878.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 396; 614 S.E.2d 79; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 420; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 1768



June 6, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 268 Ga. App. 231, 601 S.E.2d 708.
Smith v. State, 268 Ga. App. 231, 601 S.E.2d 708, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 794 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with offenses including felony theft by shoplifting and misdemeanor theft by receiving. After arraignment, the State amended the accusation. At trial, due to the fact that defendant had not been arraigned after the amendment, a nolle prosequi was entered. The trial court denied defendant's plea of former jeopardy on the later indictment. The Court of Appeals (Georgia) affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court held that defendant, by taking the position that the amended accusation was a superseding charging instrument, induced any error in the trial court. Thus, the intermediate appellate court found that the amended accusation was a superseding charging instrument and since defendant was not arraigned after the amendment, he was not put in jeopardy at trial. The appellate court found that the trial court's action in permitting the entry of a nolle prosequi was not attributable to defendant. The trial court erred in permitting the entry of a nolle prosequi after jeopardy attached and defendant, in light of his objection and request for a remedy to perceived state of the case that would not have resulted in an acquittal as a matter of law, did not induce the error. Amendment of the accusation did not start a new prosecution, the previous arraignment was sufficient, and jeopardy attached before the nolle prosequi was entered over defendant's objection. Consequently, prosecution of the offenses charged in the accusation was barred by former jeopardy. The trial court's denial of defendant's plea of former jeopardy was error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

273 of 777 DOCUMENTS



105 Floyd Rd., Inc. v. Crisp County


S05A0373.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 345; 613 S.E.2d 632; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 378; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 1556



May 23, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at 105 Floyd Rd., Inc. v. Crisp County, 279 Ga. 825, 620 S.E.2d 826, 2005 Ga. LEXIS 662 (Ga., Oct. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] County development code; constitutional question. Crisp Superior Court. Before Judge Forrester.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business sought review of a judgment from a Georgia trial court, which granted appellee county's request to permanently enjoin the business from operating, based on a finding that it qualified as a sexually-oriented adult use because its "substantial business purpose" was to sell sexually-explicit material and it had no permit pursuant to Crisp County, Georgia, Unified Land Development Code § 3.01.02.


OVERVIEW: The business purchased the leasehold and assets of a prior business that primarily sold sexually-explicit materials (SEM) to a mostly male clientele. The prior business had been denied a special use permit to operate a sexually-oriented adult use (SOAU). Thereafter, the new business reduced the inventory of SEM and added adult-themed but non-SEM that catered to a broader clientele. The county sought injunctive relief after the business began operating without a special use permit, asserting that a permit was needed because the business qualified as a SOAU due to its "substantial business purpose" of offering SEM for sale. The trial court rejected constitutional challenges to the Development Code, and permanently enjoined the business's operation. On appeal, the court found that the definition of a SOAU, based on the finding of the requisite substantial business purpose, was void for vagueness under the due process clauses of the Georgia and U.S. Constitutions, as there was no fair notice or objective standards for business owners regarding whether they needed to meet the permit requirements, nor were there clear guidelines for enforcement purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

274 of 777 DOCUMENTS



McKenzie v. State


S05A0298.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 265; 626 S.E.2d 77; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 295; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 1398



April 26, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Right to free speech; constitutional question. Forsyth State Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court (Georgia) denied demurrers challenging the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 46-5-21(a)(1), defendant stipulated to the evidence and was convicted in a bench trial of twice violating § 46-5-21(a)(1). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 46-5-21(a)(1) impermissibly infringed upon his right to free speech protected by the First Amendment and Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. V. The state's highest court agreed that the statute was an overbroad infringement on the right to free speech. Expression that was indecent but was not obscene was protected speech. The statute lacked the precision that the First Amendment required when a statute regulated the content of speech. It did not contain the necessary language setting out the least restrictive means to further a compelling state interest. Instead of applying only to obscene speech, it applied to speech that was merely indecent. Instead of making illegal such speech only when directed at minors, it made such speech illegal when heard by adults. Instead of applying only to speech not welcomed by the listener and spoken with intent to harass, it applied to speech welcomed by the listener and spoken with intent to please or amuse. Because the statute was an overbroad infringement on the First Amendment's guarantee of freedom of speech, defendant's convictions for violating the unconstitutional statute were reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

275 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Roberts v. Burgess


S05A0095.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 486; 614 S.E.2d 25; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 297; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 1383



April 26, 2005, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied June 30, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Issuance of driver's license; constitutional question. Crawford Superior Court. Before Judge Wilcox.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver administratively challenged appellee Georgia Department of Motor Vehicle's (DMVS) decision to refuse to renew the driver's license. The driver's challenge to O.C.G.A. § 40-5-22(c)(2) and (7) failed both at the administrative level and before the trial court (Georgia). The driver's application for discretionary appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: The driver was a Georgia resident with a Georgia license whose Florida license had been revoked for driving under the influence. The state's highest court distinguished persons affected by § 40-5-22(c)(2) from Georgia residents who lacked a negative out-of-state driving record. The issuance of the Georgia license was error. Further, the driver was not similarly situated to Georgia drivers whose licenses were revoked. Section 40-5-22(c)(2) did not create a suspect class or impact a fundamental right for equal protection purposes. There was a rational basis to create a class of driver's license applicants whose out-of-state licenses were suspended or revoked. The classification bore a direct relation to the strong governmental interests in protecting the public from drivers whose licenses had been revoked and in preventing license shopping. The driver's equal protection challenge to § 40-5-22(c)(7) also failed. The driver voluntarily subjected himself to Florida's laws and his Florida license was validly suspended. Neither state was precluded from taking into account offenses that occurred in another state in deciding whether to issue or revoke an already issued driver's license.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

276 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Franklin v. State


S05A0002.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 150; 611 S.E.2d 21; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 227; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 924



March 28, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] County nuisance ordinance; constitutional question. Cherokee Superior Court. Before Judge Gober, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was cited for creating a nuisance due to an accumulation of refuse on her property, in violation of Cherokee County, Ga., Code of Ordinances § 46-61(d). The trial court (Georgia) convicted defendant, after a jury trial, and sentenced her to a fine and a probated sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague. The state's highest court held that "litter" and "rubbish" were defined in the county code. While the two definitions were not all-inclusive, they provided examples of the type of substances that could not be accumulated without creating a nuisance. The examples provided adequate guidance so that it could be readily ascertained whether an item was litter or rubbish. While litter and rubbish might be subjective, such uncertainties did not render the statute void for vagueness. The statute gave sufficient warning so that individuals could avoid doing that which was forbidden. It also could be readily ascertained whether a person was "accumulating" a quantity of rubbish or litter on their property. Defendant lacked standing to claim that the ordinance improperly delegated the decision as to what constituted an accumulation of litter to local law-enforcement authorities. The ordinance did not restrict defendant's use of land without a substantial governmental interest as it clearly protected the public health, safety and welfare. Finally, the State satisfied its burden to establish venue beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Perkinson v. State


S04P1845.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 232; 610 S.E.2d 533; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 168; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 754



March 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied April 14, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Perkinson v. Georgia, 546 U.S. 896, 126 S. Ct. 229, 163 L. Ed. 2d 214, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6520 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Bartow County trial court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of malice murder, three counts of felony murder, aggravated battery, two counts of aggravated assault, two counts of false imprisonment, theft by taking, possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendant received a death sentence.

Martin v. Henry County Water & Sewerage Auth.


S04A1795.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 197; 610 S.E.2d 509; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 158; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 663



March 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied April 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation; constitutional question. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Craig.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a condemnation action, a special master awarded appellant landowners damages as just and adequate compensation for their land. Dissatisfied with the award, the landowners appealed to the superior court. There, a jury awarded them $ 400 more in damages, but granted appellee county attorney's fees, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 22-2-84.1. The landowners sought further review, and the instant matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners challenged the judgment entered against them, first contending that the trial court erred by ruling against their claim that O.C.G.A. § 22-2-84.1 was unconstitutional. The appeals court disagreed. Under the special master method, the actual taking of the condemnee's property was authorized to occur before the resolution of any value issue raised by a condemnee on appeal. Further, because the right to take an appeal to superior court and have a jury trial on the value issue was a matter of legislative grace, the legislature was free to impose conditions on the exercise of the right to appeal. Second, the landowners were not denied due process by a denial of their motion for a continuance to review 64 pages of billing records, as they were previously notified of the intent to offer the same into evidence and made no request for discovery regarding the issue. Finally, the instruction given on the issue of temporary inconvenience properly allowed the jury to determine whether the loss of the trees on the location of the temporary easement was a loss special to the landowners and thus compensable.


OUTCOME: The judgment rendered by the superior court was affirmed.

 

279 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Woods v. State


S05A0448.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 28; 608 S.E.2d 631; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 119; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 353



February 7, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sentencing; constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Lewis, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from a Georgia trial court, convicting him of criminal attempt to possess marijuana with intent to distribute under O.C.G.A. § 16-13-33. The trial court denied defendant's motion to declare § 16-13-33 unconstitutional and to impose sentence under O.C.G.A. § 16-4-6. Accordingly, defendant was sentenced under O.C.G.A. § 16-13-33 to 10 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested during a reverse undercover sting operation for the sale of a large amount of marijuana. When the undercover detective asked to see the money, defendant and another drove up and showed the money to him. As the arresting officers moved in, defendant's passenger opened fire and was killed by return shots fired by police. Defendant fled but was shortly captured. He was convicted and sentenced, and he appealed. The court first determined that defendant's constitutional challenge to O.C.G.A. § 16-13-33, which was made shortly after the guilty verdict was returned, was timely. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. The court found that defendant had abandoned his constitutional arguments by failing to provide citation or authority or argument in support thereof, leaving only his claim involving the rule of lenity. However, the court found that there was no violation of that rule, as O.C.G.A. §§ 16-13-33 and 16-4-6 were mutually exclusive. Accordingly, O.C.G.A. § 16-13-33 rendered O.C.G.A. § 16-4-6 inapplicable, as the former was applicable specifically to offenses involving the Georgia Controlled Substances Act, O.C.G.A. § 16-13-20 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
