Lewis v. State


S04A2006.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


279 Ga. 69; 608 S.E.2d 602; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 123; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 355



February 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied March 7, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lewis v. Ga., 546 U.S. 987, 126 S. Ct. 571, 163 L. Ed. 2d 478, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8017 (U.S., Oct. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wright.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried as an adult under O.C.G.A. § 15-11-28 and was convicted by the trial court (Georgia) for malice murder, felony murder, and aggravated assault, after his motion for a mistrial was denied. He was sentenced to life in prison for malice murder, with the aggravated assault conviction merging as a matter of fact and the felony murder conviction being treated as surplusage. Defendant's new trial motion was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 15-11-28 was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that defendant waived any constitutional claims. Evidence that defendant approached a car, exchanged words with the victim, produced a rifle, and shot the victim two times at point-blank range, killing him as his children watched, was sufficient to support the conviction. The trial court did not err by failing to sua sponte rule on defendant's competency. The request that competency hearings be mandated for children who faced trial as adults was rejected. The prosecutor improperly asked a witness whether he was aware that defendant told his mother that he "only shot him twice." Hearsay testimony from two police officers was improperly admitted. The jury was improperly instructed that it could infer the intent to kill from the use of a deadly weapon. However, the errors were harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of guilt. The trial court took corrective measures after the first reference to defendant's pre-trial silence and defendant failed to request a curative instruction or a mistrial after the second. Finally, trial counsel was not ineffective as the decisions were reasonable or strategic.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

281 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Hall v. Vargas


S04A1910.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 868; 608 S.E.2d 200; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 36; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 165



January 18, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Vargas v. Hall, 544 U.S. 1040, 125 S. Ct. 2271, 161 L. Ed. 2d 1072, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4072 (U.S., May 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus. Tattnall Superior Court. Before Judge Rahn.
Vargas v. State, 184 Ga. App. 650, 362 S.E.2d 461, 1987 Ga. App. LEXIS 2337 (1987)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A warden sought review of the judgment of a habeas court (Georgia), which granted a prisoner's habeas petition, holding that the trial court erred in allowing two witnesses to testify in defendant's trial on charges of molestation about an outcry made by the victim after the last instance of her alleged molestation because O.C.G.A. § 24-3-16 could not be applied in any trial for a crime committed before the effective date of the statute.


OVERVIEW: After the prisoner's convictions on three counts of aggravated child molestation were affirmed on appeal, the prisoner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that since the acts of molestation with which he was charged preceded the effective date of § 24-3-16, which permitted the State to introduce evidence in the form of hearsay statements attributed to a child victim, the trial court improperly permitted the two witnesses to testify about the victim's outcry. The habeas court granted the petition. On appeal, the court found that § 24-3-16 was not subject to the prisoner's ex post facto challenge because it did not alter the degree, or lessen the amount or measure of the proof, which was made necessary to conviction when the crime was committed. According to the court, when the prisoner committed the alleged acts of aggravated child molestation, the State was required to prove that he committed that crime as it was then defined, and the prosecution had exactly that same evidentiary burden as to the elements of aggravated child molestation when he was brought to trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the habeas court.

 

282 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Bell v. Austin


S04A2004.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 844; 607 S.E.2d 569; 2005 Ga. LEXIS 24; 2005 Fulton County D. Rep. 127



January 10, 2005, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hearsay rule; constitutional question. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant van driver sought review from a judgment of the trial court, which was entered in favor of appellees, an injured car driver and her husband, in their tort action arising from a collision. The trial court had overruled the van driver's objection to the admissibility of a narrative medical report from one of the car driver's physicians, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 24-3-18(a). The matter was transferred from the Georgia Court of Appeals.


OVERVIEW: The van driver struck the car driver from behind, causing her injuries. Appellees gave a timely pre-trial notice that they intended to introduce the medical report pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 24-3-18(a), and the trial court overruled the van driver's objection thereto. After the jury verdict was rendered in favor of appellees, the van driver sought review. The matter was transferred by the court of appeals because the appeal raised constitutional issues. The court initially found that the oath of O.C.G.A. § 24-9-60 was not implicated due to the admissibility of the medical report under O.C.G.A. § 24-3-18(a). Further, there was no denial of the van driver's right to cross-examine the physician, and he had ample opportunity to determine the expert qualifications of the medical professional. The van driver lacked standing to raise an equal protection challenge on behalf of the non-medical professionals whose reports were not excluded from the hearsay rule, and there was no due process violation because the reports which were admissible under § 24-3-18 were clearly delineated. There was no racial motive found in appellees' juror strikes, and the evidence supported the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

283 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Getkate v. State


S04A1014.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 585; 604 S.E.2d 838; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 957; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3574



November 8, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prohibition against appeal bond; constitutional question. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge McGarity.
Getkate v. State, 269 Ga. App. 558, 604 S.E.2d 611, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 1219 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was found guilty in the trial court (Georgia) of child molestation and aggravated child molestation, and was sentenced to serve 10 years in prison, followed by 30 years' probation, he moved for an appeal bond. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said O.C.G.A. § 17-6-1(g), which precluded the trial court from granting him an appeal bond, violated the separation of powers provision of Ga. Const. art. I, § 2, para. 3 because it invaded the province of the judiciary. The supreme court held there was no constitutional right to an appeal bond, and Georgia's system for allowing prisoners to be released on bond pending an appeal was a legislative function. Therefore, when the Georgia General Assembly established the parameters of such bonds, it did not invade a judicial function, and the statute it enacted to carry out this purpose did not violate the concept of separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

284 of 777 DOCUMENTS



O'Kelley v. Cox


S05A0236.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 572; 604 S.E.2d 773; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 953; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3406



October 26, 2004, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Perdue v. O'Kelley, 280 Ga. 732, 632 S.E.2d 110, 2006 Ga. LEXIS 465 (Ga., July 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Legislative process, judiciary encroachment upon. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Russell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a complaint against defendant, seeking to enjoin defendant from putting a proposal for a constitutional amendment on the general election ballot. The Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) denied the relief and dismissed the complaint. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the proposed amendment, if approved by the electorate, could not itself withstand a constitutional attack. The court held that, while the judiciary was vested with the power to determine the constitutionality of legislation, at present there was simply no legislation which could have been the subject of a constitutional attack. All that existed was a resolution of the general assembly proposing that the Georgia Constitution be amended. The judiciary was not authorized to interfere in the constitutional amendment process and prevent the voters from expressing their approval or disapproval of the proposal which their elected representatives determined should have been submitted to them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

285 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Wolcott v. State


S04A1590, S04A1591.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 664; 604 S.E.2d 478; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 941; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3448



October 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied November 22, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Probation revocation; constitutional question. Forsyth Superior Court. Before Judge Bagley.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Georgia trial court convicted defendant on charges of terroristic threat and criminal trespass in one indictment, and to a count of burglary in another. For each of these three crimes, he received first offender treatment and a probated sentence. The court later revoked his probation in each of the two cases. Defendant thereafter appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgments entered against him, first contending that the filing of the petitions by his probation supervisor was unauthorized because O.C.G.A. § 42-8-29 violated the constitutional principle of separation of powers. The appeals court disagreed, holding that the probation supervisor's duty extended only to making her findings and report thereon in writing to the court with her recommendation. By filing the revocation petitions, she did not initiate any new criminal action in the trial court against defendant. Further, the petitions invoked the continuing jurisdiction that the trial court already exercised pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 42-8-34(g). Second, the petitions filed against defendant were sufficient to comply with due process requirements, and in neither case was defendant unable to adequately prepare his defense. Third, although the trial court violated O.C.G.A. § 24-3-10, said error was harmless as any inadmissible hearsay was merely cumulative of the admissible probative testimony. Finally, the fact that defendant was not represented by an attorney in the prior revocation proceedings did not affect the admissibility of the orders entered therein.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

286 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Botts v. State


S04A0798, S04A0799.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 538; 604 S.E.2d 512; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 946; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3422



October 25, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hate crime penalty statute; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Arrington.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants moved to dismiss the sentence enhancement, contending that the hate crime penalty statute, O.C.G.A. § 17-10-17, violated their rights under the First, Fifth, Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments and the corresponding sections in the Georgia Constitution. The trial court (Georgia) denied their motions and sentenced defendants pursuant to § 17-10-17. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, along with a third individual, were indicted on charges of aggravated assault and other crimes arising out of the beating of the victims. Pursuant to the notice provisions of the hate crime penalty statute, O.C.G.A. § 17-10-18, the State served defendants with notice of the State's intent to seek sentence enhancement based on the State's allegation that defendants selected their victims because of racial bias and prejudice. However, absent some qualification on "bias or prejudice," O.C.G.A. § 17-10-17 was left so vague that persons of common intelligence had to necessarily guess at its meaning and differed as to its application. Accordingly, the appellate court held that § 17-10-17 was too vague to justify the imposition of enhanced criminal punishment for its violation. Also, § 17-10-17 could not be upheld because it impermissibly delegated basic policy matters to policemen, judges, and juries for resolution on an ad hoc and subjective basis, with the attendant dangers of arbitrary and discriminatory applications. Because the enhancement statute was unconstitutionally vague, it violated defendants' due process rights and their sentences were improper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgments.

Riley v. State


S04P1039.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 677; 604 S.E.2d 488; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 943; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3437



October 25, 2004, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied November 22, 2004.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Riley v. Georgia, 544 U.S. 1002, 125 S. Ct. 1937, 161 L. Ed. 2d 778, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 3592 (2005)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Humphrey v. Riley, 291 Ga. 534, 731 S.E.2d 740, 2012 Ga. LEXIS 696 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Newton Superior Court. Before Judge Ott.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments and sentences from the trial court (Georgia), which convicted him of three counts of malice murder and two counts of first-degree arson and sentenced him, upon the jury's recommendation, to death for each murder after finding beyond a reasonable doubt seven statutory aggravating circumstances pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 17-10-30(b)(2), (7). The trial court also denied his motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: A fire broke out in the trailer where defendant lived with his girlfriend, a friend, and his three children, two girls ages six and three, and a five-year old boy. All three adults escaped the fire. All three children died. Defendant confessed to police, after he waived his Miranda rights, that he set fire to his son's bedding while his son was asleep, intending to scare his girlfriend and planning to return and put out the fire, but that the smoke and flames "got to" the children. Neighbors and firefighters reported that defendant did not try to save his children, that his demeanor was cold, and that he moved his car away from the trailer. Defendant was convicted of malice murder and sentenced to death for each of the murders. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not err by limiting a psychologist's testimony concerning false confession theory because the knowledge that a false confession could be obtained from a suspect by police was not beyond the ken of the average juror; and it was implicit in the jury charges on the voluntariness, credibility, and corroboration of a defendant's statement to the police under O.C.G.A. §§ 24-3-50, 24-3-53.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and sentences.


 

288 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Hines v. Ga. Ports Auth.


S03G1813, S03G1821, S03G1820, S03G1848.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 631; 604 S.E.2d 189; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 838; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3318; 2005 AMC 111



October 12, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied November 22, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 262 Ga. App. 591, 585 S.E.2d 883.
Ga. Ports Auth. v. Andre Rickmers Schiffsbeteiligungsges mbH & Co. K.G., 262 Ga. App. 591, 585 S.E.2d 883, 2003 Ga. App. LEXIS 931 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff longshoreman sued defendants Georgia Ports Authority, its employee, and a ship owner in the trial court for personal injuries. The owner sought contribution from the Ports Authority and its employee. The trial court denied motions of the Ports Authority and its employee to dismiss, and the Court of Appeals (Georgia) barred claims against the Ports Authority, but let claims against the employee proceed. Further review was sought.


OVERVIEW: The longshoreman's injury occurred on a ship in navigable waters while he was engaged in traditional maritime activity. The supreme court held the Ports Authority was immune under the Georgia Constitution, but admiralty law preempted this and any state procedural requirements, and governed the longshoreman's claim and his wife's loss of consortium claim. The Authority was not an arm of the State for Eleventh Amendment immunity purposes, because it was self-sufficient and not intertwined with the State's treasury. Factors of state law and state control tended to weigh towards a finding of no immunity. This was not contrary to finding the Authority was entitled to state-conferred sovereign immunity as a state court decision that the Authority was a state "agency" for state immunity was different from finding under federal law that the Authority was not an "arm of the state" for Eleventh Amendment immunity purposes. Because the Authority was not immune under the Eleventh Amendment, and the ship owner's contribution and indemnity claim was recognized in admiralty and maritime law, there was no bar to that claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was reversed.

 

289 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Thompson v. State


S04A0699.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 394; 603 S.E.2d 233; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 793; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3130



September 27, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 42-1-13; constitutional question. Worth Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought to revoke defendant's probation. Defendant, who pled guilty to child molestation, was granted discretionary review of an order entered by the trial court (Georgia), which upheld the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 42-1-13, found defendant in violation of the statute, and continued defendant's probation provided that he relocate to a new residence within 10 day.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 42-1-13 was an unconstitutional ex post facto law when applied to him as the statute went into effect while defendant was on probation. Defendant had lived in a house located within 303 feet of a municipal community center for over 15 years and his continued residence in that house violated the statute. The appellate court held that § 42-1-13 was not being applied retrospectively. Section 42-1-13 did not alter the consequences for the offense of child molestation; rather, it created a new crime based in part on an offender's status as a child molester. The new statute did not increase the punishment meted out to previously convicted sex offenders. It did not punish sex offenders retrospectively on the basis of their status. It simply declared that convicted sex offenders who currently resided within certain well-defined areas were guilty of a felony. If a convicted offender violated the statute, he could be prosecuted (or have his probation revoked) for that current violation. Defendant was being punished for currently violating § 42-1-13 by refusing to move. Defendant's new crime sparked his probation revocation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

290 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Poppell v. Gault


S04A1330.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 437; 603 S.E.2d 271; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 806; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3120



September 27, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. McIntosh Superior Court. Before Judge Rahn.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant magistrate brought a petition in mandamus against appellee county commissioners, seeking a writ compelling the commissioners to pay him the annual salary, allowances, and supplements he had been receiving before the commissioners reduced his salary to that of a part time magistrate. The trial court (Georgia) denied the petition. The magistrate appealed.


OVERVIEW: After becoming aware of testimony in a separate lawsuit that the magistrate worked in the office only two days a week, the commissioners began paying the magistrate a part-time salary. The appellate court held that a governing authority was allowed to reduce the amount it paid a chief magistrate when the greater amount was not the amount due the recipient. There was evidence that the magistrate was no longer regularly exercising the powers of a magistrate at least 40 hours a week, and he declined to certify the number of actual hours he did work. A chief magistrate working less than full-time was not entitled to the salary of a full-time chief magistrate. The trial court did not rule on the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 15-10-23(a)(3), and the appellate court declined to address the issue because it did not rule on a challenge to the constitutionality of a statute unless the issue was raised and ruled on in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

291 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Mann v. State


S04A1454.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 442; 603 S.E.2d 283; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 814; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 3148



September 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Mann v. Ga. Dep't of Corr., 282 Ga. 754, 653 S.E.2d 740, 2007 Ga. LEXIS 849 (Ga., Nov. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OCGA § 42-1-13; constitutional question. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Simmons.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Georgia) denied appellant probationer's request for declaratory relief that would hold O.C.G.A. § 42-1-13, the Residency Statute, which prohibited registered sex offenders from living within 1,000 feet of specified places, unconstitutional. The probationer appealed.


OVERVIEW: In August 2003, the probation officer of the probationer notified him that he would be required to vacate his residence because he was living within 1,000 feet of a child care facility in violation of § 42-1-13. The probationer filed suit, arguing that § 42-1-13 was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that whatever minimal property interest the probationer might have had in residing in his parent's home was substantially outweighed by the State's interests underlying the Residency Statute. The Residency Statute had very little economic impact on the probationer and there was no evidence that the probationer had any investment-backed expectations relative to the property. In no sense did the Residency Statute's application impose a burden upon the probationer that should have been borne by society-at-large. Thus, the appellate court rejected the probationer's claim that the Residency Statute permitted the regulatory taking of property without just and adequate compensation. In addition, the appellate court found that § 42-1-13 was not unconstitutionally vague. Also, the appellate court found that O.C.G.A. § 42-1-12, the Registered Offender Statute, was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Albany Surgical, P. C. v. Ga. Dep't of Cmty. Health


S04A1359.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 366; 602 S.E.2d 648; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 627; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 2937



September 13, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Separation of powers doctrine; constitutional question. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Lockette.
Albany Surgical, P.C. v. Dep't of Cmty. Health, 257 Ga. App. 636, 572 S.E.2d 638, 2002 Ga. App. LEXIS 1246 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical company challenged a decision by a trial court (Georgia), which entered summary judgment for defendant Georgia Department of Community Health (DCH) on the company's declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that Ga. Comp. R. & Regs. Rules 272-2-.01(19)(h)(3) and 272-2-.09(1)(b)(10) were unconstitutional. A prior summary judgment decision in DCH's favor was affirmed on appeal without deciding the constitutional issue.


OVERVIEW: The company brought an action for a declaration that the DCH's regulations requiring a Certificate of Need for ambulatory surgical centers were invalid. A prior summary judgment in favor of the DCH was affirmed on appeal, but the case was remanded for a determination of the constitutional issues that the company raised, but that the trial court did not rule on. The trial court again granted summary judgment in the DCH's favor, finding that the regulations were constitutional. The company appealed, arguing that the procedure for approving the regulations under O.C.G.A. § 31-6-21.1 violated the separation of powers doctrine under Ga. Const. art. 1, § 2, para. 3 by allowing a proposed regulation to become effective by legislative inaction. It also claimed that the procedure violated the bicameralism and presentment provisions of Ga. Const. art. 3, § 5, para. 5. The court held that the legislature was empowered to delegate rule making authority to administrative agencies and O.C.G.A. § 31-6-21.1 did not invest the legislature with executive powers or vice versa, so there was no separation of powers problem. As regulations were not laws, the bicameralism provision was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment grant in favor of the DCH.

Quarterman v. Douglas County Bd. of Comm'rs


S04A1339.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 363; 602 S.E.2d 651; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 628; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 2940



September 13, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. Douglas Superior Court. Before Judge Howe.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed petitions against appellees, the Douglas County Board of Commissioners members and the Development Authority of Douglas County, seeking a temporary restraining order and writs of prohibition and mandamus to restrain the collection of the Special Purpose Local Option Sales Tax (SPLOST) and to require appellees to vacate a bond project. The trial court (Georgia) granted appellees' motion to dismiss. The resident appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that the denial of his request to intervene in the SPLOST's validation proceedings was improper. The appellate court found that the taxpayer had both actual knowledge and statutory notice of the validation proceedings and did not request to intervene. Further, the taxpayer did not appeal from a denial of intervention or the validation judgment. Thus, the taxpayer was precluded from claiming error in the statement of the required appeal bond. Further, the taxpayer was precluded by O.C.G.A. § 36-82-78 from collaterally attacking the validation judgment. § 36-82-78 included within its scope the security for revenue bonds. The intergovernmental contract between the Board and the Authority had been held to be a legal, valid, binding, and enforceable obligation of the county. The validation judgment was conclusive as to the validity of the revenue bonds and the intergovernmental contract. Even if the validation judgment was unconstitutional, arguably void, or obtained by fraud, accident, or mistake, it could not be collaterally attacked with respect to either the revenue bonds or their security.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

294 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Robinson v. State


S04A0265.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 134; 598 S.E.2d 466; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 524; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 2146



June 28, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Peremptory juror challenges; interim review. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Collier.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with malice murder, felony murder, burglary, aggravated battery, and other offenses. The State sought the death penalty. In a pretrial motion, the State requested that the trial court (Georgia) rule that O.C.G.A. § 15-12-165, which granted a criminal defendant twice as many peremptory juror challenges as the State, was unconstitutional. After a hearing, the trial court granted the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that because defendant's case involved a male defendant and two female victims, one of whom was deceased, the defense would have stricken women because they were women and that the State would have stricken men because they were men. The State surmised that, since O.C.G.A. § 15-12-165 gave defendant twice as many peremptory strikes, after each side exercised 10 peremptory strikes, defendant would continued to have stricken females from the jury while the State, having exhausted all its peremptory strikes, would have been unable to strike males. The appellate court found that the Equal Protection Clause prohibited discrimination in jury selection on the basis of gender. If either party exercised any peremptory challenges with alleged discriminatory intent, a remedy already existed in the form of a Batson/J.E.B. motion. Because the law provided a remedy for jurors who were struck for illegal reasons by the defense, the order of the trial court erred in finding O.C.G.A. § 15-12-165 unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

295 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Earl v. Mills


S04A0181.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 128; 598 S.E.2d 480; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 525; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 2123



June 28, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Creation of judgeships; constitutional question. Cherokee Superior Court. Before Judge Langford, Senior Judge.
Earl v. Mills, 275 Ga. 503, 570 S.E.2d 282, 2002 Ga. LEXIS 875 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county resident appealed from the entry of summary judgment in favor of appellee chief judge, on remand, in the resident's challenge to a second standing order entered by the chief judges of the superior and state courts and the presiding judge of the juvenile court of the Blue Ridge Circuit (Georgia), which requested judicial assistance from the juvenile court judges in certain domestic matters.


OVERVIEW: The resident argued that the request for assistance resulted in the unconstitutional creation of judgeships. The appellate court held that requesting and receiving intra-county assistance did not create a judgeship. The juvenile court judges who assisted the superior court did not become superior court judges. Thus, no judicial position constitutionally required to be filled by election or by gubernatorial appointment until election was created by the exercise of O.C.G.A. § 15-1-9.1(b)(2). Further, § 15-1-9.1(b)(2) did not authorize the judiciary to make appointments to the bench, but provided the means to permit a judicial officer from one court to exercise the power of a requesting court in limited circumstances. The request was neither an unconstitutional creation of a class of court nor an unconstitutional usurpation of legislative authority. The request was pursuant to § 15-1-9.1(b)(2)(C) as the request was for a specified time of limited duration and any court could withdraw from participation after giving 30 days' notice. Finally, the superior, state, and juvenile courts did not take permanent action by requesting judicial assistance that spanned two terms of court.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was vacated insofar as the trial court ruled on the constitutionality of the creation of permanent judicial assisting positions. The summary judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

McLeod v. Columbia County


S04A0696.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 242; 599 S.E.2d 152; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 537; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 2120



June 28, 2004, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied July 29, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Utility charge; constitutional question. Columbia Superior Court. Before Judge Overstreet.
McLeod v. Columbia County, 254 F. Supp. 2d 1340, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5140 (S.D. Ga., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sued appellee Columbia County (Georgia), seeking a judgment declaring that a storm water utility charge the County imposed was unconstitutional and an order enjoining the County from collecting the charge. The County filed a counterclaim, seeking payment of unpaid charges. The Columbia County Superior Court (Georgia) granted the County's motion for summary judgment, and the owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board of Commissioners of Columbia County adopted a storm water management ordinance which created the Columbia County Stormwater Utility. People who owned developed property in the district were assessed a monthly storm water utility charge based on the amount of impervious surface area located on their property, and four owners filed an action against the County, seeking a declaration that the charge was unconstitutional. The trial court held that the charge was a fee, not a tax, and it dismissed the lawsuit. The state supreme court held that (1) pursuant to Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, para. III(a)(6), and general statutory law, the County was authorized to establish the utility and to impose a charge for storm water management services; (2) the County was not required to establish a community improvement district before it established the utility; (3) the storm water utility charge was not an invalid tax; and (4) the County's method of apportioning the costs of storm water services was not arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgments granting summary judgment in favor of the County with respect to the property owners' constitutional claims and the County's counterclaim for unpaid charges.

 

297 of 777 DOCUMENTS




Lamar v. State


S04P0328.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 150; 598 S.E.2d 488; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 536; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 2151



June 28, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Douglas Superior Court. Before Judge James.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Douglas County Superior Court (Georgia) denied defendant's request to represent himself, he was convicted of murder and related crimes, and the jury fixed his sentence for the murder conviction at death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant did not know what he faced. The supreme court held defendant was mentally competent. The trial court asked him about his knowledge of the law, rather than finding if he knowingly and intelligently waived his right to counsel by telling him of the dangers of self-representation, as required. He had a sound general knowledge of the charges and the trial process; grasped the dangers of self-representation explained to him; and knew the benefit counsel could provide. He knowingly and voluntarily waived counsel and unequivocally asserted his right to represent himself. He could be retried, as the evidence let a rational trier of fact find him guilty on each charge beyond a reasonable doubt and find at least one statutory aggravating circumstance. He could ask prospective jurors if they were conscientiously opposed to a life sentence with parole and would consider that sentence for murder. O.C.G.A. § 15-12-142(a) let the trial court sequester the jury over defendant's objection. O.C.G.A. § 17-7-130.1, providing for defendant's examination by a court-appointed psychiatrist or psychologist, was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were reversed, and the matter was remanded for a new trial.


 

298 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Brown v. Kroger Co.


S03G1231.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 65; 597 S.E.2d 382; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 454; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 1870



June 7, 2004, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied June 28, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia.
Brown v. Kroger Co., 2003 Ga. LEXIS 855 (Ga., Oct. 6, 2003).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party filed a personal injury action against appellee business. The case was dismissed for want of prosecution, and the State Court of Fulton County (Georgia) entered an order confirming the dismissal. The injured party refiled her action, but the trial court granted the business's motion for summary judgment. The Court of Appeals of Georgia dismissed the injured party's appeal, and the state supreme court granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: An injured party filed suit against a business on August 11, 1995, alleging that she was hurt when a store the business owned was robbed. Five years later, the case was automatically dismissed for want of prosecution, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-11-41(e). On July 20, 2001, the trial court entered an order confirming the dismissal for want of prosecution, and on September 17, 2001, the injured party refiled her action as a renewal of her lawsuit. The business filed a motion for summary judgment, and the trial court granted the motion. The state supreme court held that O.C.G.A. § 9-2-60 gave the injured party six months to refile her lawsuit after it was dismissed, and the trial court ruled correctly that the six-month period began on August 11, 2000, the date the lawsuit was automatically dismissed pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-11-41(e), not on July 20, 2001, the date the trial court entered its order confirming the fact that the lawsuit had been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

299 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Ciak v. State


S04A0343.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 27; 597 S.E.2d 392; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 468; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 1909



June 7, 2004, Decided.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Use of tinted automobile windows; constitutional question. Cobb State Court. Before Judge Darden.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress all evidence derived from a traffic stop, based on an officer's suspicion that defendant violated O.C.G.A. § 40-8-73.1. Defendant was then granted interlocutory review to address the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress, rejecting the argument that O.C.G.A. § 40-8-73.1 applied only to residents of Georgia, as defendant was not situated similarly to a class being treated differently, and the legislature legitimately applied piecemeal remedies to achieve the statute's purpose of promoting the safety of law enforcement personnel. The appeals court disagreed with both holdings. Because non-residents could be as dangerous as residents, no rational connection existed between the residence of the driver of a vehicle and the goal of improving law enforcement officer safety during traffic stops. Thus, the distinction drawn by the statute violated the constitutional guarantee of equal protection of the laws because it distinguished between similarly situated persons, drivers of cars registered in Georgia, on a basis which bore no reasonable relation to the purpose of the statute. However, the unconstitutionality of the statute did not require suppression, as the officer observed defendant's car, noted that the windows were tinted a dark purple, and believed the tinting appeared darker than that permitted by § 40-8-73.1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

300 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Bauerband v. Jackson County


S04A0226.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 222; 598 S.E.2d 444; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 472; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 1878



June 7, 2004, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied July 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Local government debt limitation; constitutional question. Jackson Superior Court. Before Judge Overstreet from Augusta Circuit.
Bauerband v. Jackson County, 2004 Ga. LEXIS 555 (Ga., June 7, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county residents challenged a decision from a trial court (Georgia), which granted a motion by appellee county board of commissioners for summary judgment dismissing the residents' challenge to the county's decision to enter into a lease purchase agreement with the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia (ACCG) to finance and construct a new courthouse.


OVERVIEW: The county planned to enter a lease agreement with the ACCG to help finance and construct a new courthouse. The proposed agreement was designed to comply with O.C.G.A. § 36-60-13. The residents sued to prevent the county from proceeding with the agreement, arguing primarily that the agreement resulted in the county incurring debt without a public vote, contrary to the mandate of Ga. Const. art. IX, § V, para. I(a). When summary judgment was granted to the county, the residents appealed. They argued O.C.G.A. § 36-60-13 was not constitutional and that the leases, as applied and in effect, would violate either the constitution or the statute because the leases would constitute a debt lasting for more than year. The court found its prior decisions were binding precedent that O.C.G.A. § 36-60-13 was constitutional. Moreover, the county's power to terminate the contract, included for compliance with § 36-60-13, was not meaningless simply because a decision to terminate would be difficult. Finally, the lease did not bind future county commissioners and it did not created a debt of more than a year that would be subject to the voting requirement in Ga. Const. art. IX, § V, para. I(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment grant in favor of the county.

 

301 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Dixon v. State


S04A0072.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


278 Ga. 4; 596 S.E.2d 147; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 343; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 1888



May 3, 2004, Decided.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied June 4, 2004. As Amended June 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Aggravated child molestation; constitutional question. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Matthews.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the trial court (Georgia) convicted defendant of misdemeanor statutory rape and aggravated child molestation, but acquitted him of rape, false imprisonment, aggravated assault, and sexual battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendant, age 18, forcibly raped the victim, age 15. Defendant was less than three years older than the victim was. The defense claimed that the act was consensual. The appellate court found that the legislative intent was to prosecute the conduct that occurred in this case as misdemeanor statutory rape. The legislature amended O.C.G.A. § 16-6-3(b) such that conduct meeting the criteria of the misdemeanor statute could only have been punished as a misdemeanor. It would have been incongruous with that legislative intent if the State retained the discretion to prosecute the exact same conduct as either misdemeanor statutory rape or felony child molestation, O.C.G.A. § 16-6-4(c). O.C.G.A. § 16-6-3(b) was more specific, and thus prevailed over the more general O.C.G.A. § 16-6-4(c). Further, O.C.G.A. § 16-6-3(b) was the most recent legislative judgment regarding the appropriate punishment for defendant's conduct. Since the legislature most recently declared that sex between teenagers less than three years apart was to be punished as misdemeanor statutory rape, and not felony child molestation, that judgment prevailed.


OUTCOME: The conviction for aggravated child molestation was reversed.

 

302 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Lindsey v. State


S04A0224.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 772; 596 S.E.2d 140; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 319; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 1531



April 27, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Carrying a concealed weapon; constitutional question. Atlanta City Court. Before Judge Jackson.
Lindsey v. State, 259 Ga. App. 389, 577 S.E.2d 78, 2003 Ga. App. LEXIS 108 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with carrying a concealed weapon, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-126(a). Defendant was convicted after a bench trial in the Fulton County City Court (Georgia), but in an earlier appeal, the appellate court remanded for a ruling on defendant's constitutional challenge to O.C.G.A. § 16-11-126(a). The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the law, and overruled defendant's general demurrer. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During a search of defendant's vehicle, a gun was found in the pocket door on the passenger side. Defendant argued that O.C.G.A. § 16-11-126(d) was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court found that when the language of O.C.G.A. § 16-11-126(d) was given its commonly understood meaning, it authorized the transportation of a gun in an auto so long as it either was fully exposed to the view of others or, in the alternative, was placed in the glove compartment, console, or in a similar closed compartment which was beyond the immediate access of the car's occupants. If the weapon was only exposed to the view of some or was not located in a closed compartment, it was not being lawfully transported within the meaning of the statute. The trial court properly overruled defendant's demurrer. The gun was accessible to an occupant of the car, but was not fully exposed to the view of others. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

303 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Keck v. Harris


S03A1425.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 667; 594 S.E.2d 367; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 266; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 1003



March 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Domestic relations. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Stedman, pro hac vice. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-14-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-20-02. Lower Ct # :011036124.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father brought a complaint for, inter alia, modification of child support payable to appellee mother, and in connection therewith sought a determination that Georgia's Child Support Guidelines, O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15, was invalid under the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution. The Cobb County Superior Court (Georgia) upheld the constitutionality of the Child Support Guidelines. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court erroneously entered a certification of its order pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 9-11-54(b) since the order did not dispose of any claim, but only determined that the single claim for modification was to be resolved in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15. However, the appellate court treated the certification as one entered pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 5-6-34(b). The appellate court found that the majority of the constitutional arguments advanced by the father were considered by the appellate court in an earlier case in which it held that O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15 was not unconstitutional under the Supremacy Clause. If Georgia had not reviewed its guidelines in the exact manner stated in 45 C.F.R. § 302.56 (h), it did not "do major damage" to that federal interest. Because Georgia's child support guidelines plan, O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15, and amendments thereto had been approved by the United States Secretary of Health and Human Services as being in conformity with the federal statutory scheme, the appellate court deferred to that determination. The father acknowledged that O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15 had been upheld against challenges on due process, equal protection, and privacy grounds.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

304 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Ward v. McFall


S03A1365.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 649; 593 S.E.2d 340; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 179; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 759



March 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 19, 2004.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McFall v. Ward, 543 U.S. 818, 160 L. Ed. 2d 26, 125 S. Ct. 57, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5647 (U.S., Oct. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Child support guidelines; constitutional question. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Nation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In post decree proceedings, appellee mother filed a complaint to modify child support and visitation, and moved for a declaration that the Georgia Child Support Guidelines found in O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15(b) were unconstitutional. The trial court (Georgia) set the mother's child support amount and declared that O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15 was invalid. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that Georgia had completely failed to abide by 45 C.F.R. § 302.56(h), and therefore held that Georgia's child support guidelines were invalid. The trial court found that O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15 was inconsistent with the federal regulation, and therefore, in violation of the Supremacy Clause of the Constitution of the United States. The appellate court found that appellate jurisdiction was properly with the appellate court. Since there was no Congressional statement of pre-emption, nor was this an area in which Congress left no room for states to act, the question of pre-emption revolved around the issue of whether the child support guidelines, and the method by which they were reviewed, were an obstacle to Congressional goals. The federal interest was in obtaining child support orders to enforce the obligations of non-custodial parents. If Georgia had not reviewed its guidelines in the exact manner stated in 45 C.F.R. § 302.56 (h), it did not do major damage to that federal interest. Further, the Secretary of Health and Human Services had approved and certified Georgia's plan. O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15 was not unconstitutional under the Supremacy Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Strykr v. Long County Bd. of Comm'rs


S04A0223.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 624; 593 S.E.2d 348; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 187; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 761; 2004-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P74,316



March 1, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] County ordinance; constitutional question. Long Superior Court. Before Judge Cavender.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident sued defendant county, asking the trial court (Georgia) to permanently enjoin and strike as unconstitutional the amendments to the county's sold waste services ordinance that authorized the county to enter into a contract with a private enterprise for the provision of garbage collection services. The trial court denied the resident's petition. The resident appealed.


OVERVIEW: The resident first argued that the ordinance violated antitrust prohibitions. The appellate court found that local government entities were immune from antitrust laws when engaged in conduct pursuant to state policy. The alleged anticompetitive conduct was conduct expressly contemplated by the Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq. Whether the contract was beneficial and necessary to the residents was a question properly for determination by the county's commissioners. O.C.G.A. § 12-8-21(a) was not violated by provisions in the ordinance authorizing the termination of a resident's collection service for nonpayment of the collection fee. Because only the amendments to the county's solid waste ordinance were placed in the record, the appellate court could not address the resident's constitutional arguments challenging alleged language in portions of the ordinance not pled and proved. The appellate court could not address complaints about the legal organ of the county because that entity was not a named party to the case, nor did the resident seek to join it in the proceedings below.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

306 of 777 DOCUMENTS



I.D.K., Inc. v. Ferdinand


S03A1359


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 548; 592 S.E.2d 673; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 70; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 412



February 2, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Regulation of adult entertainment establishments; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, adult entertainment establishments and their employees, sought review of a judgment of the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) concerning appellee county's ordinance requiring any person working at an adult entertainment establishment that served alcohol to obtain a permit from the county tax commissioner. Appellants had sought an injunction and a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The purpose of the ordinance was to regulate adult establishments to reduce criminal activities and to promote the protection and development of neighborhoods. The ordinance was enacted after public hearings, studies of other jurisdictions, and evidence of problems within the county. The court affirmed. The evidence established that the purpose of the ordinance was to combat secondary effects associated with adult entertainment establishments, which made the ordinance content-neutral. As a content-neutral ordinance, it could be upheld if it furthered an important government interest. The ordinance dealt with the important government interest of controlling criminal behavior and was a proper exercise of the county's police power. The fact that a fee was charged for the permit was not an unconstitutional prior restraint because the fee merely reimbursed the costs of administering the permit program. Appellants' equal protection claim, based on an argument that the ordinance was content-based, failed because the ordinance was content-neutral and such ordinances could be used to regulate adult entertainment establishments differently from other businesses.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

307 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Banks v. State of Ga.


S03A1282, S03A1414.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 543; 592 S.E.2d 668; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 71; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 419



February 2, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Forfeiture. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hunter.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in Case Number S03A1282. Judgment reversed in Case Number S03A1414.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court upheld the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. § 16-13-49(s)(1), and entered an order of forfeiture, in two separate cases. The forfeiture relied in part upon the hearsay evidence admitted at the hearing. The court also ruled that a search warrant executed at defendant's home was supported by probable cause. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgments entered. The appeals court first held that the purpose of the testimony provided by the officers at the forfeiture hearing was to explain the basis for seeking a warrant to search defendant's house. Thus, the testimony was admissible for such a limited purpose. However, while the police had probable cause to believe that a completed or attempted armed robbery or aggravated assault occurred at defendant's home, they had probable cause to believe that evidence related to those offenses, such as blood and hair, would be found in the house. However, they did not have sufficient reliable information to believe that defendant was selling drugs from the home. Informants were not named, and the affiant admitted that he had no personal knowledge of whether these individuals were truthful. Further, the record showed that cocaine and money were both found in closed containers which were not opened until a dog brought to the premises for the express purpose of searching for drugs alerted his handler to their presence. Under the circumstances, discovery of these items was the product of an unauthorized search for drugs.


OUTCOME: The appeal from the original order of forfeiture was dismissed. However, in a second order of forfeiture, the constitutionality finding was affirmed, but the probable cause finding and forfeiture of the contraband seized was reversed.

Collins v. State


S04A0122.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 586; 591 S.E.2d 820; 2004 Ga. LEXIS 23; 2004 Fulton County D. Rep. 186



January 12, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 13, 2004.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Collins v. Humphrey, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17794 (S.D. Ga., Mar. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder, post-conviction appeal. Richmond County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Albert Pickett. Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-21-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-12-02. Lower Ct #: 96RCCR1276.
Collins v. State, 273 Ga. 30, 538 S.E.2d 34, 2000 Ga. LEXIS 769 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the judgment of the Richmond County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied appellant's motion to have his conviction and sentence declared null and void.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of malice murder. His conviction was affirmed on appeal. In seeking relief, appellant claimed that his conviction and sentence were null and void because "aforethought" was an essential element of malice murder and the trial court's purported instruction to the jury that Georgia law did not require premeditation prohibited the jury from making a finding regarding the element of premeditation and relieved the State of its burden of proof with regard to that element. The trial court denied appellant's motion after finding that it failed to raise any discernable justiciable issue. Appellant then filed a direct appeal, invoking Ga. 309 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Robles v. State


S03A0582.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 415; 589 S.E.2d 566; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 1018; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3499



November 26, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Collier.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court convicted defendant of felony murder and cruelty to a child in connection with the death of her son. Defendant later moved for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged her convictions, raising numerous claims of error. The appeals court found none had merit. First, the verdicts were not mutually inconsistent. Even accepting that they were, the evidence was sufficient to support them. Second, jurors were not presumed to be pro-State merely by reciting the pledge of allegiance. Rather, a juror's willingness to recite the pledge, with its reinforcement of the concepts of liberty and justice for all, showed no bias for either side. In fact, such was more likely to remind a juror of his or her obligations in the pursuit of justice. Third, there was no abuse of discretion surrounding the jurors which were struck for cause, due to the inability to stand in judgment of another, a belief that the law was unequally applied, and for another's religious beliefs. Fourth, witnesses were properly qualified and accepted as experts. Fifth, a Jackson-Denno hearing was not required, as defendant's statement was introduced for purposes of impeachment. Finally, the indictment sufficiently informed defendant of the charge to allow her to prepare an intelligent defense.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.
