Union County v. CGP, Inc.


S03A0669, S03X0670.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 349; 589 S.E.2d 240; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 994; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3384



November 17, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus. Union Superior Court. Before Judge Langford, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case No. S03A0669. Judgment affirmed in Case No. S03X0670.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer sued defendant county seeking a declaration of its rights and a writ of mandamus forcing the county to issue the desired building permits. The trial court (Georgia) denied mandamus, but declared that the developer had a vested right to complete the subdivision without complying with the flood ordinance, and ordered the issuance of building permits on that basis. The county appealed and the developer cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The developer obtained various approvals in relation to his proposed development of a retirement community, including building permits for six houses. When the developer sought more building permits, they were refused. The developer was told that no more permits would be issued until the subdivision was in compliance with a flood ordinance as recently amended. On appeal, the supreme court concluded that it had jurisdiction over the matter since the appeal was one from a grant of mandamus. In addition, the supreme court concluded that unofficial approval of the developer's plans without regard to the restrictions of the flood ordinances would have frustrated the county's duty to its residents to enforce the law. On cross-appeal, the developer asserted that the trial court erred in rejecting its attacks on the validity of the floor ordinances. The developer argued that the ordinances were void based on the county's failure to give residents sufficient notice and an opportunity to be heard. The supreme court found evidence that other forms of notice other than publication were used and thus, the developer failed to bear its burden of showing the unconstitutionality of the ordinances.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that the developer had a vested right to complete its development free of restrictions imposed by the flood ordinance was reversed. The trial court's denial of the developer's claim regarding the validity of the ordinance was affirmed.

 

311 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Hamilton v. Renewed Hope, Inc.


S03A1369.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 465; 589 S.E.2d 81; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 999; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3392



November 17, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 12, 2003.
Appeal after remand at Hamilton v. Renewed Hope, Inc., 2006 Ga. LEXIS 934 (Ga., Nov. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Service by publication; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shoob.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Georgia) granted summary judgment to appellee assignee of a tax sale purchaser of real property for a decree in quia timet under O.C.G.A. § 23-3-40 et seq. that it held title to the property, while it denied summary judgment to appellant property owner, who had sought a declaratory judgment that she could redeem the property after the redemption period in the notice served on her by publication had expired. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner did not live in the subject property, but rented it to tenants. This was the only address in the tax and deed records on the property, and the assignee was allowed to serve notice of the foreclosure of the owner's right to redeem by publication. The supreme court held the use of public records to find the owner's address was necessary, but other efforts were required when notice mailed to the last known address available from the tax or deed records was returned as undeliverable. The majority rule requiring the assignee, before resorting to publication of the required notice, to make reasonably diligent efforts beyond the use of tax and real estate records to ascertain the owner's address, was adopted. There was no evidence that the assignee tried to find the owner's address from any source other than tax and deed records, that other channels were not reasonably available, or that use of them would have been impractical, so it was not entitled to summary judgment. There was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the owner's address was reasonably ascertainable, so the owner was not entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment denying the owner's summary judgment motion was affirmed, but the trial court's judgment granting the assignee's summary judgment motion was reversed.

 

312 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Greater Atlanta Homebuilders Ass'n v. DeKalb County


S03A0552.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 295; 588 S.E.2d 694; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 935; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3300



November 10, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Tree protection ordinance; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hunter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff development associations filed an action against defendant county challenging a tree ordinance. The trial court (Georgia) upheld the ordinance. The associations appealed.


OVERVIEW: The associations contended that the ordinance was invalid because it was not enacted in accordance with the Zoning Procedures Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1, et seq., which imposed minimum due process standards upon local governments when they adopted or amend zoning ordinances. The supreme court concluded that the ordinance, viewed as a whole, did not regulate according to zones or districts. The ordinance's limited references to zoning areas did not turn the ordinance into a zoning ordinance since the requirements applied to all land regardless of location. The associations also argued that the ordinance effected a regulatory taking of their property with just compensation. As the associations failed to show that they were deprived of all economically viable use of their land, the supreme court upheld the validity of the ordinance. Finally, the associations argued that the ordinance was pre-empted by O.C.G.A. § 12-6-24, which related to commercial timber harvesting. The supreme court concluded that state law did not pre-empt the ordinance since the legislature made it clear that the § 12-6-24 did not preclude counties from enacting and enforcing tree ordinances.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

313 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Perkins v. State


S03A1325.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 323; 588 S.E.2d 719; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 954; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3326



November 10, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bond recovery agents, registration of; constitutional question. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Bessen.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from a trial court (Georgia), which denied his motion to dismiss an accusation that charged him with attempting to capture a principal on a bail bond without registering as a bail recovery agent with the local sheriff in violation of O.C.G.A. § 17-6-58(a), and with criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: A professional bail bondsman hired defendant to act as a bail recovery agent. In 2001, defendant was assigned to apprehend a principal on a bond issued by the bondsman. Defendant located the principal in a Fulton County apartment and kicked in the door to make an arrest. Defendant had been registered as a bail recovery agent in the county in 2000; however, his registration was not renewed for 2001. Subsequently, defendant was charged with violating O.C.G.A. § 17-6-58(a). Defendant argued that § 17-6-58(a) was unconstitutionally applied to him. The court agreed, holding that the county's failure to maintain a system for the registration of individual agents precluded a successful prosecution of defendant for violating § 17-6-58(a). Also, defendant could not be held vicariously liable for the bondsman's alleged failure to register defendant in violation of O.C.G.A. § 17-6-56(c). Because O.C.G.A. § 17-6-58(a) did not make it a crime to fail to renew a registration, that provision did not provide defendant with fair notice that he could be held criminally responsible for acting as a bail recovery agent in the county if he failed to renew his registration in that county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying defendant's motion to dismiss the accusation.

 

314 of 777 DOCUMENTS



City of Decatur v. DeKalb County


S02G1617.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 292; 589 S.E.2d 561; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 934; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3312



November 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Judgment entered by City of Decatur v. DeKalb County, 267 Ga. App. 214, 598 S.E.2d 926, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 592 (2004)
On remand at, Appeal after remand at DeKalb County v. City of Decatur, 2007 Ga. App. LEXIS 972 (Ga. Ct. App., Aug. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 255 Ga. App. 868.
City of Decatur v. DeKalb County, 255 Ga. App. 868, 567 S.E.2d 332, 2002 Ga. App. LEXIS 796 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari to determine whether a decision by the Court of Appeals (Georgia) properly interpreted the Homestead Option Sales Tax Act (HOST), O.C.G.A. § 48-8-100 et seq. Plaintiff cities had filed an action against defendant county, alleging claims for breach of contract and attorney fees, arising from an alleged failure by the county to properly disburse funds under HOST to the various cities.


OVERVIEW: The county voters approved a tax under HOST, and to facilitate the capital outlay requirement, the county entered into an intergovernmental agreement with several cities inside the county. However, the cities disputed the amount of money that the county was to disburse to them. Accordingly, the cities commenced their action against the county. The trial court granted the county's motion for judgment on the pleadings, holding that the agreement was void. The court of appeals affirmed that judgment, holding that HOST required that the county administer the tax funds and that it could not shift that responsibility to the cities pursuant to the agreement. On certiorari review, the court held that the court of appeals had relied on case precedent in error. The court concluded that HOST implemented a district tax under the "special district" provision of Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, para. VI, which was not a "county tax" as described in the judicial precedent relied upon. Accordingly, distribution of the proceeds from the county to the cities was allowable. The court noted that a ruling on whether the agreement was authorized under Ga. Const. art. IX, § III, para. I was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

315 of 777 DOCUMENTS



BellSouth Telecomms., Inc. v. Cobb County


S03A1220.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 314; 588 S.E.2d 704; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 949; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3298



November 10, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Telecommunications ordinance; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Kreeger.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court granted summary judgment to appellee county after finding that state statutory law gave the county the "necessarily implied authority" to enforce its ordinance that allowed the county to charge appellant telecommunications company, and other telecommunications companies, a one-time permit fee in order to use the county's public rights-of-way. The telecommunications company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The telecommunications company applied to use the county's public rights-of-way. The county, pursuant to one of its ordinances, imposed a one-time permit fee on the telecommunications company, as it did on all telecommunication company applicants. The telecommunications company filed an action in the trial court to challenge the county's authority to enforce the ordinance and declare the ordinance unconstitutional. The trial court found that O.C.G.A. § 32-4-42 gave the county the "necessarily-implied authority" to charge telecommunications companies a permit fee as a means of regulating a telecommunications company's installation of lines on the county's rights-of-way so long as the fee was reasonably related to the regulation. It then found the ordinance was a reasonable regulation because it involved an administrative cost recoupment fee for the cost in reviewing permit applications, as opposed to a tax intended to produce revenue for the county. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the permit fee was reasonably related to the regulation and the evidence showed that the telecommunications company's equal protection rights had not been violated by the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

316 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Hardin v. State


S03A1238.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 242; 587 S.E.2d 634; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 889; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3121



October 20, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Search and seizure; constitutional question. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the trial court (Georgia), which convicted him of trafficking in methamphetamine and driving without a license on his person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped at a police roadblock while driving a borrowed vehicle. He did not have a driver's license on his person. He gave an officer permission to search his vehicle. The officer found a bag of methamphetamine. The court held that O.C.G.A. § 16-13-31(e) did not violate equal protection of the laws because the statute contained no purity requirement, as was required for cocaine. The legislature was under no duty to treat all drugs and drug offenders the same. The mere fact that cocaine and methamphetamine were both listed as Schedule II controlled substances did not mean that the legislature had to enact identical statutes pertaining to those substances. The statute treated all those charged with methamphetamine trafficking equally. Defendant's detention and search at the police roadblock was not an unconstitutional search and seizure because the roadblocks were implemented as safety checkpoints based on a number of citizen complaints about drunken and reckless drivers in the area. It was unnecessary to determine whether the police had proper probable cause to search defendant's vehicle because he voluntarily consented to the search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

317 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Head v. Stripling


S03A0525.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 403; 590 S.E.2d 122; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 1053; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3657



October 14, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 26, 2003. Reconsideration Denied November 26, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Stripling v. Head, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3810 (U.S., May 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Head v. Stripling, 588 S.E.2d 226, 2003 Ga. LEXIS 856 (Ga., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The habeas court (Georgia) vacated the inmate's death sentence imposed following a jury's finding that he was guilty of crimes arising out an armed robbery at his place of employment in which two employees were killed. Respondent warden appealed.


OVERVIEW: The warden challenged the habeas court's ruling vacating the inmate's death sentence, ordering that the inmate be sentenced to a non-capital sentence based on a finding that his death sentence was a miscarriage of justice because he was mentally retarded, and that O.C.G.A. § 17-7-131 was unconstitutional to the extent that it required the inmate to prove his mental retardation beyond a reasonable doubt in the guilt-innocence phase of a death penalty trial. The supreme court held, inter alia, that the State violated Brady, requiring that the inmate be granted a new trial, by suppressing parole records that contained material, exculpatory evidence regarding the inmate's mental retardation, that the habeas court erred by finding the inmate mentally retarded since such a determination should have been left to a jury, and that § 17-7-131 was constitutional and the inmate was required to bear the burden of proving his alleged mental retardation beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the habeas court was affirmed as to the order requiring a new trial and reversed as to the finding that the inmate was mentally retarded beyond a reasonable doubt and as to the order requiring imposition of a non-capital sentence, and as to the Patillo claim.

 

318 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Fortson v. State


S03A1169


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 164; 587 S.E.2d 39; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 840; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2999



October 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Fortson v. State, 2006 Ga. LEXIS 196 (Ga., Mar. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Madison County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Lindsay A. Tise, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-27-03. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-24-03. Lowert Ct. # : 00MCR141JT.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from her conviction by the Madison County Superior Court (Georgia) of malice murder, attempted arson, and related crimes, challenging the denial of her motion for a change in venue, the denial of her motion to suppress, and the denial of her motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that she received ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions. The victim was found encased in concrete in a cattle trough on a farm defendant used for hunting. Defendant had purchased 10 80-pound bags of concrete and a cattle trough. Defendant's mailbox was painted the same as the trough, and the paint was found in defendant's home. However, defense counsel ineffectively represented defendant, as he used a peremptory strike to strike a juror who had been stricken for cause. Defendant was prejudiced by the unnecessary waste of a peremptory strike. The search warrant for defendant's home was supported by probable cause under the totality of the circumstances. Witnesses had observed defendant at the victim's home near the time he disappeared. The farm manager who located the victim's body told police that defendant used the farm for hunting. The victim had a tumultuous relationship with defendant. Because the search warrant for the house was proper, the evidence obtained from the truck was not tainted as "fruit of the poisonous tree."


OUTCOME: The convictions were reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for a new trial.

 

319 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Cooper v. State


S03A1255.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 282; 587 S.E.2d 605; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 842; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3004



October 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Implied consent statute; constitutional question. Barrow Superior Court. Before Judge Booth.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the trial court (Georgia) for driving under the influence of cocaine, challenging the denial of his motion to suppress blood test results taken after an accident with his consent after he was read his rights under O.C.G.A. § 40-5-55(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the implied consent provision allowed the State to require a person to consent to a search of his bodily substances without probable cause. The State's highest court held that the provision violated the Georgia and U.S. Constitutions. While special needs exceptions to the probable cause requirement had been recognized, the implied consent provision's purpose was primarily to gather evidence for a criminal prosecution. No matter how important that purpose might be, it did not create a special need to depart from the probable cause requirement. The implied consent provision compelled chemical testing merely due to involvement in a traffic accident resulting in serious injury or death, and did not require probable cause of impaired driving. Defendant was not under arrest when he was read the implied consent notice, and the trooper's sole basis for administering the blood test to him was because he believed that O.C.G.A. § 40-5-55(a) mandated that he do so. The trooper did not find probable cause that defendant was driving in violation of O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391, and defendant's consent was invalid. The blood test results should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The denial of the suppression motion was reversed. Defendant was granted a new trial.

 

320 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Sheriff v. State


S03G0492


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 182; 587 S.E.2d 27; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 844; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2983



October 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Judgment entered by Sheriff v. State, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 458 (Ga. Ct. App., Mar. 31, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia.
Sheriff v. State, 258 Ga. App. 423, 574 S.E.2d 449, 2002 Ga. App. LEXIS 1470 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, by writ of certiorari, the affirmance by the Court of Appeals (Georgia) of the trial court's interpretation of O.C.G.A. § 17-8-70 as prohibiting two defense attorneys from making the closing argument on his behalf.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the appellate court improperly overruled Limbrick v. State. The state's highest court agreed. O.C.G.A. § 17-8-70 was construed under the substantive law in effect when the 1982 Code was enacted. Section 17-8-70 was construed such that the statutory limitation of one counsel "heard in conclusion" applied to the party exercising the privilege of the final jury argument chronologically. That construction harmonized all parts of the statute and gave a sensible and intelligent effect to each part of the statute. The first part of § 17-8-70 provided that two attorneys could present argument on behalf of a party without leave of court. If the second part of the statute was construed as limiting the middle and concluding argument to one attorney, it rendered the first part meaningless. White v. Cline, 330 S.E.2d 386 (1985), and its progeny were overruled to the extent they limited the number of counsel who might present the middle argument. Ga. Unif. Super. Ct. R. 13.3 and the Uniform State Court Rules were to be similarly construed. It was error to limit the number of defense attorneys who could participate in the middle argument. The error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The convictions were reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for a new trial.

 

321 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Gates v. Gates


S03A1305


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 175; 587 S.E.2d 32; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 848; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2981



October 6, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Domestic relations. Peach County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. G. Bryant Culpepper. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-06-03. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-07-03. Lower Ct #: 02V0576.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an case certified for immediate review by the trial court, which was transferred by the Georgia Court of Appeals to the state's highest court, appellant husband appealed from the denial of his motion to dismiss, which had been treated as a motion for summary judgment, alleging that appellee wife's claim for damages for personal injuries arising from a motorcycle accident was barred by interspousal tort immunity.


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the interspousal tort immunity doctrine applied, even though one count of the wife's complaint requested a divorce. The supreme court held that the interlocutory appeal involved only a tort claim, and was not a divorce case within the meaning of Ga. Const. art. VI, § VI, para. III(6). Further, the wife failed to bring the matter within the constitutionality jurisdiction of the supreme court. In the interests of judicial economy, the supreme court ruled on the underlying claim. The Harris exception to application of the interspousal tort immunity doctrine was inapplicable. The wife knew about the alleged tort and the husband's role, but then extinguished her cause of action by marrying the husband. The wife did not point to any evidence which showed an extreme factual situation under Harris. The trial court erred in denying the husband's motion for summary judgment, as the husband was entitled to judgment based on the interspousal tort immunity doctrine. The doctrine, as codified in O.C.G.A. § 19-3-8, did not violate the due process or equal protection provisions of the Georgia or U.S. Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for consideration of any constitutional questions properly raised.

Head v. Hill


S03A0559, S03X0560.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 255; 587 S.E.2d 613; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 850; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 3404



October 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. (S03A0559) Butts County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. John D. Allen from Chattahoochee Circuit. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-22-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-25-02. Lower Ct #: 94V216. (S03X0560) Butts County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. John D. Allen. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-22-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-03-02. Lower Ct #: 94V216.
Hill v. State, 263 Ga. 37, 427 S.E.2d 770, 1993 Ga. LEXIS 315 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded in S03A0559. Judgment affirmed in S03X0560.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee warden sought review from an order of the Butts Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellant's motion for reconsideration of his habeas corpus petition and granted a limited writ, ordering a jury trial as to appellant's mental retardation claim based on a preponderance of the evidence standard. Appellant had previously been convicted and sentenced to death for murder, which was affirmed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: After his conviction and appeal, appellant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that he was mentally retarded. The trial court granted the writ to the limited extent of ordering a jury trial on the question of mental retardation, using the "preponderance of the evidence" standard. On appeal, the court reversed, and on remand, the trial court found that appellant had not proved his mental retardation beyond a reasonable doubt, as required by O.C.G.A. § 17-7-131(a)(3). By supplemental order, the trial court denied appellant's remaining claims. Thereafter, the trial court allowed reconsideration and granted a writ on the mental retardation issue, with proof by appellant to be by a preponderance of the evidence. On appeal, the court held that Ring and Atkins did not require a jury trial on the mental retardation claim. Further, as it was originally waived at trial, the matter was only reviewable under a miscarriage of justice standard. The court found that many issues were procedurally defaulted, for which no cause and prejudice was shown, or they were barred by res judicata. Appellant failed to state a claim for ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting appellant's motion for reconsideration of the mental retardation claim. The court also affirmed the trial court's denial of relief to appellant on all other grounds.

Jones v. State


S03A0608


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 36; 586 S.E.2d 224; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 722; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2746



September 15, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Manis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) of felony murder and possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime. The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment on the felony murder conviction and a consecutive five-year term of imprisonment on the firearm possession conviction. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A witness testified he heard defendant and the victim arguing in a hallway. The witness then heard a gunshot and found the victim's body in the hallway. A gun, which an expert testified was the murder weapon, was found under a carpet in defendant's room. The supreme court found that (1) the evidence was sufficient; (2) the trial court did not err in permitting expert testimony that the atomic absorption test for gunpowder on defendant's hand was verifiably certain and in admitting the test results into evidence; (3) the trial court's use of "consistent" in its curative instructions following defendant's motion for mistrial did not assume certain things as fact and did not intimate to the jury what the judge believed the evidence to be; (4) the trial court properly did not permit a defense witness to give opinion testimony regarding an experiment she had conducted at the crime scene; (5) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for mistrial; (6) defendant could not complain of the jury charge to which he agreed; and (7) the charge given by the trial court was a correct statement of the law, and the failure to use defendant's suggested language was not error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

324 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Perdue v. Baker


S03A1154


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


277 Ga. 1; 586 S.E.2d 606; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 700; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2700



September 4, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1]
Perdue v. Baker, 276 Ga. 822, 2003 Ga. LEXIS 699 (Ga., July 15, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Attorney General of Georgia, refused the request of petitioner, the Governor of Georgia, to dismiss an appeal to the U.S. Supreme Court filed on behalf of Georgia in a case involving legislative reapportionment under the Voting Rights Act. The Governor sought a writ of mandamus compelling the Attorney General to dismiss the appeal. The Georgia trial court denied the Governor's petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed a law reapportioning state senate districts. A federal district court declined to give the plan preclearance under § 5 (42 U.S.C.S. § 1973c) of the Voting Rights Act; the Attorney General appealed to the U.S. Supreme Court. Meanwhile, the legislature enacted a revised plan, 2002 Ga. Laws 149 (Act 444); the new districts would take effect only if the prior act was held to violate the Voting Rights Act. In denying the Governor relief, the trial court ruled that the Attorney General had exclusive authority to decide whether to continue the appeal. The state supreme court rejected the Attorney General's claim that the instant appeal became moot when the U.S. Supreme Court vacated the federal district court's judgment and remanded the case. First, that federal case was still pending; second, the issue was one of significant public concern, was capable of repetition, and had evaded review. Under the constitution and statutes, neither officer had the exclusive power to decide the State's interest in litigation. By declining to dismiss the appeal, the Attorney General was fulfilling a duty required by Act 444. Act 444 did not violate separation of powers principles.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

325 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Morrison v. State


S03A0049.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 829; 583 S.E.2d 873; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 618; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2188



July 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 29, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Morrison v. Georgia, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2105 (U.S., Mar. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mental retardation, burden of proof. Richmond Superior Court. Before Judge Mulherin, Senior Judge.
Morrison v. State, 258 Ga. 683, 373 S.E.2d 506, 1988 Ga. LEXIS 474 (1988)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court convicted defendant of rape, armed robbery, and murder and sentenced him to death. The convictions and sentence were affirmed on appeal. Defendant thus alleged he was mentally retarded, and the habeas court remanded the case for a hearing on the issue. Upon a finding that he was not retarded, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the finding that he was not mentally retarded and could thus be executed. However, no error was found. Defendant committed prior crimes that required specific planning, intelligence, and logistics. Also, he attended school until about the ninth grade, and his school and juvenile records were devoid of any indication that authorities suspected he might be mentally retarded. The crime scene photographs showed the restraints defendant attempted to use on the murder victim and the ransacking of the house, due to his attempt to find and steal items of value. These photographs supported the State's version of the crime scene and illustrated the resourcefulness displayed by defendant to accomplish his criminal purposes. The given instructions properly informed the jury that a verdict of mental retardation would not result in the defendant's release from custody. The trial court did not err by refusing to charge the jury that a verdict of mental retardation would result in a life sentence. Finally, the procedure requiring defendant to prove his mental retardation by a preponderance of the evidence in a jury trial was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

326 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Langlands


S03A0162.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 721; 583 S.E.2d 18; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 602; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2037



June 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Langlands v. State, 2006 Ga. LEXIS 389 (Ga., June 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to suppress, etc.; constitutional question. Stephens Superior Court. Before Judge Cornwell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Stephens County (Georgia) trial court with (1) murder, (2) felony murder, (3) aggravated assault, (4) possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony and (5) possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress a custodial statement and sustained his demurrer to two counts of the indictment. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant did not validly waive counsel when certain custodial statements were made. The supreme court held this was not clearly erroneous, as an officer encouraged defendant to speak after he invoked his right to counsel. Defendant's charge of possession of a firearm by a felon, on which a charge of felony murder was predicated, was based on defendant's Pennsylvania misdemeanor conviction for involuntary manslaughter, which carried a maximum five-year sentence. O.C.G.A. § 16-11-131, criminalizing a felon's firearm possession, gave insufficient notice to defendant that his Pennsylvania misdemeanor could be a predicate felony for a charge under the statute. O.C.G.A. § 16-11-131(a)'s definition of a felony created an ambiguity, in that a person of ordinary intelligence could fail to appreciate that the statute intended to encompass any offense with a maximum penalty over 12 months, even if it was called a misdemeanor. Had sufficient notice been given, the Full Faith and Credit clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1, would not prohibit according defendant's misdemeanor conviction felony status.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

327 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Campbell v. State Rd. & Tollway Auth.


S03A0160.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 714; 583 S.E.2d 32; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 610; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2013



June 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Issuance of revenue bonds; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Barnes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court denied objections to the state's petition to validate and approve issuance of specific bonds used for highway construction and which were to be repaid from federal grants made to the state. It also found a joint resolution between appellees, a state department and a state authority, to allow the state authority to issue the bonds was constitutional. It then validated and approved the bonds. Appellant taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: A bill was enacted to allow the State Road and Tollway Authority (SRTA) to issue specific bonds to fund highway construction and to use future federal-aid highway funds to retire the bonds. Thereafter, the SRTA and the State Transportation Board entered into a joint resolution that approved road projects, gave the SRTA power to issue the bonds, and provided the SRTA would pay the bonds from the federal-aid highway funds. The state then petitioned to confirm and validate issuance of the specific bonds. The taxpayers argued that validation violated the Georgia Constitution. The trial court disagreed, and validated and approved the bonds. After the taxpayers appealed, the state supreme court found the joint resolution did not violate the certain-contracts-prohibited clause because the resolution was not a binding contract pledging the state's credit or imposing obligations on the state's treasury, did not violate the gratuities clause because the use of federal highway funds for the projects substantially benefited the state and its citizens, and did not violate the annual appropriations provision since a state authority could constitutionally receive federal-aid highway funds.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

328 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Mohamed v. State


S03A0083


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 706; 583 S.E.2d 9; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 604; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2028



June 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Financial transaction card theft; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Adams, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the trial court (Georgia) of financial transaction card theft. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Another's credit cards were found on defendant, and O.C.G.A. § 16-9-31(d) said a person's possession of two or more financial transaction cards issued to one other than the person's family without the cardholder's consent was prima facie evidence of a financial transaction card theft. The supreme court held this provision created an unconstitutional burden-shifting presumption, and a jury instruction stating the provision was not harmless, as evidence of defendant's guilt was not overwhelming. The unconstitutional provision was severable from the rest of the statute, and the evidence allowed defendant's retrial. The cards were discovered on defendant's person in a valid pat-down search. Defendant's cross-examination of the arresting officer was not unduly limited when defendant could not ask the officer if his testimony at a suppression hearing satisfied the requirements for a legal search. Defendant's requested instructions to the effect that the State had to show defendant deliberately withheld the cards from the victim were covered by other instructions. The trial court's instruction on the consequences of a failure to achieve unanimity should not have been given.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, and the matter was remanded for a new trial.

 

329 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Napier v. State


S03A0007. S03A0009.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 769; 583 S.E.2d 825; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 547; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 2489



June 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied July 11, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Morse.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments of conviction rendered by the Chatham County Superior Court (Georgia), convicting them of murder, concealing the death of another, and auto theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the trial court erred by forbidding voir dire questioning regarding their status as prison escapees and in charging the jury on certain statutory presumptions regarding venue. Because the issue of defendants' escape from prison was relevant to the subject matter of the State's prosecution, the supreme court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion by prohibiting them from raising that issue during voir dire. After reviewing the transcript, however, the supreme court concluded that based on the overwhelming evidence of defendants' guilt, it was highly improbable that this error contributed to the jury's verdicts. Therefore, it was harmless. Defendants also argued that the trial court erred by giving the jury instructions regarding venue that improperly imposed a burden on them to disprove that venue was properly laid. The supreme court concluded the charge did not raise any improper burden-shifting presumptions regarding venue, though the court did note that the legislation from which the instructions came was poorly drafted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction were affirmed.

 

330 of 777 DOCUMENTS



City of Buford v. Ga. Power Co.


S03A0089.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 590; 581 S.E.2d 16; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 475; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 1565



May 19, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equity. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Clark.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee power company filed an action against appellant city, seeking an injunction against the enforcement of a city ordinance that placed a moratorium on the construction of electric power substations. The trial court (Georgia) held that the ordinance was preempted by state law and enjoined its enforcement. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that placed a 1-year moratorium on the construction of electric power substations within 500 feet of residentially zoned property. A power company began construction on a substation that violated the ordinance, and the city issued a stop work order. On appeal, the city contended that O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(5) did not apply, as the city's charter and O.C.G.A. § 36-34-2(7) authorized the city to regulate the placement of substations. The supreme court held that the city's authority under § 36-34-2(7) was limited to a utility's use of city property. The power company was not using city property. It was constructing the substation on its own property. Thus, neither the city charter nor § 36-34-2(7) gave the city authority to regulate the subject substation. The city also contended that, as the Public Service Commission (PSC) did not have rules and regulations governing the placement of substations, such building was not part of the PSC's business activity, and was thus not within the express preemption of O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(5). The supreme court concluded that the regulation of electric power substations by municipalities was preempted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

331 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Brown v. State


S03A0414


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 606; 581 S.E.2d 35; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 481; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 1585



May 19, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation; constitutional question. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Howell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State indicted defendant for the felony of selling a non-controlled substance that defendant implicitly represented to be a controlled substance, in violation of O.C.G.A. § 16-13-30.1(a)(1)(A). Defendant waived her right to a jury trial, and the trial court (Georgia) found her guilty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that her felony conviction under O.C.G.A. § 16-13-30.1(a)(1)(A) was unconstitutional because her conduct also violated O.C.G.A. § 16-13-30.2, which made it a misdemeanor to possess or distribute an "imitation controlled substance," and the State improperly prosecuted her for violating the statute with the greater penalty rather than the one with the lesser penalty. The supreme court noted that both statutes prohibited the sale of fake illegal drugs. The supreme court agreed with the court of appeals that one of the ways a person could "distribute," as that word was used in § 16-13-30.2, was by selling the fake controlled substance. The supreme court found that using the same evidence, a reasonable trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's conduct violated either the felony or misdemeanor statute. Because the same conduct constituted both a felony and a misdemeanor, the rule of lenity required that defendant be subjected to the penalties for the misdemeanor, rather than the felony.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed.

 

332 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Bd. of Pub. Educ. v. Hair


S03A0031


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 575; 581 S.E.2d 28; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 487; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 1566



May 19, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Local ordinance, etc.; constitutional question. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Bass.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A board of public education sued the county board of commissioners and tax commissioner, challenging as unconstitutional a county ordinance and state statute under which the county received a 2.5 percent commission for collecting the school taxes. The Georgia trial court upheld the ordinance and statute.


OVERVIEW: A county ordinance and state statute were constitutional, as Ga. Const. art. VIII, § 6, para. 3 and O.C.G.A. 48-5-404(a) allowed the entity that collected school taxes up to a 2.5 percent commission. When examined on a statewide basis the commission was not an unreasonable rate of reimbursement. O.C.G.A. § 48-5-404(a) did not violate Ga. Const. art. VIII, § 6, para. 3, though the charge may have been more than the county's costs to collect school taxes. Because O.C.G.A. § 48-5-404(a) did not limit the county's commission to the cost to collect the school taxes, the county ordinance that authorized the county to receive 2.5 percent did not violate the state statute. The caption of the 1994 legislation signed by the governor that amended the law at issue stated that it was an act to repeal certain obsolete and superseded laws and provisions of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated based upon classification by population. O.C.G.A. § 48-5-404(b) was a provision based on classification by population, and, therefore, was related to and had a natural connection with the main object of the legislation that effected its repeal.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

333 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Ga. Dep't of Human Res. v. Sweat


S03A0179.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 627; 580 S.E.2d 206; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 360; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 1399



April 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 2, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sweat v. Ga. Dep't of Human Servs., 157 L. Ed. 2d 310, 124 S. Ct. 432, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 7722 (U.S., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Atkinson County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Dane Perkins. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-27-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-07-02. Lower Ct#: 2000C127.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Atkinson County (Georgia) declared the statutory child support guidelines (Guidelines) under O.C.G.A. § 19-6-15, to be unconstitutional, concluding they violated the constitutional guarantees of due process, equal protection and privacy, and also operated as an unconstitutional taking of property. Appellant, the Georgia Department of Human Resources, sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court held that while the Guidelines did distinguish between custodial and non-custodial parents, that distinction was required in order to ensure that the non-custodial parent contributed his or her fair share to ensure the welfare of the children was protected. Second, contrary to the trial court's conclusion, custodial and non-custodial parents were not similarly situated. The custodial parent contributed to the costs of caring for children, and had primary responsibility for the day-to-day care of a child, to ensure he or she received adequate financial resources from the non-custodial parent. Non-custodial parents had measurably less involvement in the day-to-day care of children, and depended on the Guidelines to ensure that their support obligations were not out of proportion to their income. Third, the trial court also erred by implying that the Guidelines affected only obligors and violated the constitutional right to privacy. Fourth, the Guidelines were not a governmental taking. Finally, there was no provision that an indigent had the right to free court reporter services in an appellate, civil proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

334 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Ward v. City of Cairo


S03A0352.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 391; 583 S.E.2d 821; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 305; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 1102



March 27, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Separation of powers doctrine; constitutional question. Grady County Superior. Hon. H. Arthur McLane. Judgment Appealed March 18, 2002. Appeal Date April 15, 2002. Lower Ct. # 01V306.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judge brought an action for declaratory judgment against defendants, a city and a county, to determine the validity of contracts for probation services and the constitutionality of O.C.G.A. §§ 36-32-2(a), 42-8-100(f)(1), (g)(1). The Grady County Superior Court (Georgia) entered judgment in favor of defendants on all counts of the complaint. The judge appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the request of the judge, the county entered into a contract with a private entity which provided probation services. The judge terminated the contract. The judge was directed to reinstate the contract, but failed to comply. The judge was terminated. On appeal, the judge claimed that O.C.G.A. § 36-32-2(a) unconstitutionally violated the separation of powers doctrine because it authorized the city to control the court's day-to-day activities. The supreme court held that because the municipal court was a municipal office discharging strictly municipal functions, § 36-32-2(a) did not violate the separation of powers doctrine of the Georgia Constitution. The judge also asserted that O.C.G.A. § 42-8-100(f)(1), (g)(1) violated the separation of powers doctrine because they unconstitutionally allowed the executive to invade the province of the judiciary by requiring the governing authority's approval of the selection of a private probation service provider. Because the state court's selection of a probation services provider financially impacted the governing authority, it did not invade the province of the judiciary to attach such contract to the governing authority's approval.


OUTCOME: The trial court's entry of judgment in favor of the city and the county was affirmed.

 

335 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Columbus-Muscogee County Consol. Gov't v. CM Tax Equalization, Inc.


S02A1688.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 332; 579 S.E.2d 200; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 287; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 968



March 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by CM Tax Equalization Found., Inc. v. Columbus-Muscogee County Consol. Gov't, 157 L. Ed. 2d 142, 124 S. Ct. 288, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6248 (U.S., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ad valorem taxes; constitutional question. Muscogee County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. George M. Peagler, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-25-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-03-02. Lower Ct # :SU2000CV3256.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Muscogee County Superior Court, Georgia, granted summary judgment to plaintiff taxpayers, and against the county government defendants, in the taxpayers' suit challenging the constitutionality of a local constitutional amendment affecting the ad valorem taxation of homestead property. The county government appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the Homestead Freeze local constitutional amendment (LCA) was unconstitutional because it conflicted with the uniformity in taxation clause of the Ga. Const. art. VII, § I, para. III (1983). However, this ruling failed to recognize that pre-existing LCAs which were not repealed were to be continued in force and effect. Thus, because the LCA was a subsequent amendment to the uniformity clause, and because the LCA continued in force and effect, the LCA was valid despite any conflict with the uniformity clause. The LCA was not unconstitutional under a rational relationship equal protection analysis because of classifications it drew among homeowners based upon purchase-date classification, or because of the separate classification of homeowners and renters. Further, the LCA did not violate the Equal Protection Clause just because racial minorities had less success than their white economic counterparts in obtaining the financing necessary to purchase homes. Finally, because there was no cut-off date or durational residence requirement in the LCA, there was no violation of the right to travel guaranteed by the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Sallie v. State


S02P1702.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 506; 578 S.E.2d 444; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 279; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 980



March 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 11, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sallie v. Georgia, 540 U.S. 902, 124 S. Ct. 251, 157 L. Ed. 2d 185, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5999 (2003)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by Sallie v. Humphrey, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22006 (M.D. Ga., Mar. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Bacon County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. L. A. McConnell, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-21-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-08-02Lower Ct#: 00R073.
Sallie v. State, 269 Ga. 446, 499 S.E.2d 897, 1998 Ga. LEXIS 518 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions of malice murder, felony murder, burglary, aggravated assault, kidnapping with bodily injury, and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony, and from his death sentence in the Bacon County Superior Court (Georgia), in a second trial after his first convictions were reversed on appeal. Defendant also appealed from the denial of his motions for a new trial and to quash his indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by refusing to excuse two prospective jurors for cause. The appellate court held, inter alia, that there was sufficient evidence to support the convictions and the sentence. The prospective jurors were properly seated. The trial court did not improperly restrict defendant's voir dire questions. There was no error in the excuse of four prospective jurors for cause. Disabled persons were not systematically excluded from the grand jury. There was no error with the jury charges. Defendant was properly denied a lesser-related charge as to felony murder predicated on burglary. Any error in bias in the grand jury was harmless. The death sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor and was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The convictions and the death sentence were affirmed.

Geng v. State


S02A1313.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 428; 578 S.E.2d 115; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 244; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 1324



March 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 10, 2003. As Corrected April 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Fulton County City Court. Hon. Lenwood A. Jackson. Lower Ct. # 1531362.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Fulton County City Court (Georgia) that denied his request for a jury trial and convicted him of speeding; defendant claimed that his trial before a traffic violations bureau pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 40-13-60 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer for misdemeanor speeding in violation of O.C.G.A. § 40-6-181. Defendant's written demand for jury trial was denied, and the case was transferred to a city court traffic violations bureau for disposition pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 50-13-60. The state supreme court held that the charges were not transferred to the traffic violations bureau until after defendant's demand for a jury trial was filed. Thus, until the transfer, the case proceeded as a routine misdemeanor speeding offense and the right to jury trial attached when defendant filed his timely written demand. As a result, the provision of § 15-13-60 that limited defendant's right to a jury trial violated Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. XI. However, the offending portion of the statute could be severed without undermining the general intent of the statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

King v. City of Bainbridge


S02A1685.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 484; 577 S.E.2d 772; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 246; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 792



March 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 11, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by King v. City of Bainbridge, 157 L. Ed. 2d 138, 124 S. Ct. 228, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 7020 (U.S., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Decatur County Superior. Hon. J. Richard Porter, III. Lower Ct. # 96V040.
King v. City of Bainbridge, 272 Ga. 427, 531 S.E.2d 350, 2000 Ga. LEXIS 419 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mobile home owner sought review of a decision of the Decatur County Superior Court (Georgia), which held in favor of appellee city in the city's suit against the owner to enforce its zoning ordinance that precluded her placement of a mobile home in an R-2 residential district.


OVERVIEW: The owner placed her mobile home on her property, in violation of a city ordinance that specifically excluded mobile homes from R-2 districts. The city filed suit and after an initial reversal on a procedural ground, the trial court held that the zoning ordinance was constitutional and was not preempted by the National Manufactured Housing and Safety Standards Act of 1974, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 5401-5426. On appeal, the court agreed that the city's ordinance was not preempted by federal law and was constitutional. The court held that the ordinance was not preempted by the Act because the city had not infringed on the federal government's control over safety and construction standards for mobile homes. The testimony of a city official that a mobile home that met building codes could be placed in R-2 districts was in conflict with the ordinance and unsupported. As to the constitutionality argument, the evidence showed that the city's purpose in restricting mobile home placement was to regulate the quality of housing stock and promote general safety concerns. Those reasons were not arbitrary or unreasonable and bore a substantial relation to the public health, safety, and general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Holmes v. Traweek


S02A1665.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 296; 577 S.E.2d 777; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 248; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 787

Appellant mother moved to transfer venue to another county. The trial court denied the motion and certified its denial order for immediate review. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Georgia granted an application for interlocutory review to determine whether there was a conflict between O.C.G.A. § 19-7-22(a)'s provision that a father seeking to legitimate a child may file a petition to do so in the superior court of the county of his residence and Ga. On appeal, the court found that there was a conflict, and that the venue portion of O.C.G.A. § 19-7-22(a) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

340 of 777 DOCUMENTS



City of Atlanta v. Barnes


S02A1338, S02A1478.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 449; 578 S.E.2d 110; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 258; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 796



March 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 11, 2003.
Subsequent appeal at Barnes v. City of Atlanta, 275 Ga. App. 385, 620 S.E.2d 846, 2005 Ga. App. LEXIS 975 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Fulton County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Rowland W. Barnes. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-01-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-28-02. Lower Ct # : 2000CV24809 (S02A1338.). Lower Ct # :1998CV01491 (S02A1478.).



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, appellant city appealed from a judgment by the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) granting summary judgment to appellee class of attorneys who had paid the tax but who claimed that the city's occupation tax was unconstitutional. The city also appealed from declaratory relief granted to appellee attorney, who did not pay the tax.


OVERVIEW: The class of attorneys and the attorney contended that the tax unconstitutionally required payment of the tax before practicing law and created the possibility of incarceration of lawyers who engaged in the practice of law but refused to pay the tax. The appellate court held that the statute was unconstitutional. Payment of the tax was a precondition to the practice of law, and incarceration for practicing law without payment of the tax would impede the practice of law whether that incarceration was directly for practicing while delinquent or indirectly for that conduct by means of a contempt citation. The requirement that the tax be paid prior to practicing law could not be severed without radically rewriting the ordinance. Overruling Henderson v. Carter, 195 S.E.2d 4 (1972), the appellate court held that O.C.G.A. § 48-5-380(c) did not preclude bringing a class action for the refund of the taxes. The holding was applied retroactively, as the financial hardship to the city by a retrospective application did not alone justify prospective application. The city erroneously contended that the trial court held that the statute of limitations was tolled for the class of attorneys.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment and declaratory relief were affirmed.

 

341 of 777 DOCUMENTS



King v. State


S02A1329


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 126; 577 S.E.2d 764; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 64



January 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at King v. State, 2005 Ga. App. LEXIS 203 (Ga. Ct. App., Mar. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Search warrant, right to privacy. Gwinnett County State. Trial Judge: Hon. David M. Fuller. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-08-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-12-02. Lower Ct#: 00D036213.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence following a one-car accident. The Gwinnett County Court, Georgia, denied defendant's motion to suppress his medical records from the hospital where he was treated after the accident. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court granted defendant's interlocutory application to consider whether he was entitled to notice and an opportunity to be heard on the State's request for a search warrant to obtain his personal medical records. Because a search warrant required a neutral judicial officer to find probable cause that a crime has been committed, defendant's constitutional right to privacy was not violated when the State obtained private medical records through a search warrant without notice to defendant or a hearing on the request. Requiring pre-seizure notice and a hearing would undermine the use of search warrants in criminal investigations; it could also affect prosecutions involving other crimes and records held by third parties. The State narrowly drafted the search warrant to seek only the medical records related to the hospital's treatment of defendant on the night of his accident, and the trial court found the search warrant affidavit was legally sufficient to establish probable cause. Since the magistrate had a substantial basis for concluding that probable cause existed, the State complied with all the established procedures in obtaining the search warrant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
