Rabun County v. Ga. Transmission Corp.


S02A1374.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 81; 575 S.E.2d 474; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 4; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 140



January 13, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Local ordinance; constitutional question. Rabun Superior Court. Before Judge Struble, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee electric corporation obtained a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief as to appellant county in regard to a county ordinance. The Georgia Superior Court declared the ordinance unconstitutional under the home rule and uniformity provisions of the Georgia Constitution. The county contended the trial court erred in holding that the ordinance was void as an unconstitutional interference with the power of eminent domain.


OVERVIEW: The electric corporation distributed and transmitted electric power pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 46-3-170. It was comprised of 39 affiliated electric membership corporations and was authorized to exercise the power of eminent domain pursuant to O.G.G.A. § 46-3-201(b)(9). It began planning construction of a 115-kilovolt transmission line to service the electrical demands of the certain customers of an affiliated electric membership corporation that served the county. The electric corporation selected a particular route which crossed approximately seven miles of the county, as the site for the proposed transmission line. The county subsequently adopted a high voltage line construction moratorium ordinance. It was undisputed that the electric corporation would have to condemn property in order to effectuate the project as proposed, and that the ordinance would halt the project. The appellate court held there was simply no requirement that the electric corporation demonstrate to the county the necessity or the appropriateness of its proposed project.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

343 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Benefield v. State ex rel. Baker


S02A1736.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 100; 575 S.E.2d 453; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 5; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 173



January 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Griffin v. Keller, 2005 Ga. LEXIS 39 (Ga., Jan. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prohibition. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Struble, Senior Judge.
Griffin v. State, 241 Ga. App. 783, 527 S.E.2d 577, 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1696 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sentence Review Panel reduced a sentence imposed by appellant judge. The judge then found that the Panel lacked statutory authority and that O.C.G.A. § 17-10-6 was unconstitutional. Appellees attorney general and others sought a writ of prohibition against enforcement of the order. The trial court (Georgia) granted the writ as enforcement of that to the portion of the order that held the statute unconstitutional. The judge appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judge asserted that prohibition was not an available remedy. The state's highest court concluded that appellees were authorized to petition for a writ of prohibition on the ground that the judge lacked jurisdiction to address the constitutionality of the Panel in the context of the criminal case. The sentences that the judge initially imposed were not void and were affirmed. Under O.C.G.A. § 17-10-6(d), the judge's subject matter jurisdiction was strictly limited to determining whether the sentences for which the individual sought review were among those that the Panel was statutorily authorized to reduce. The Panel did not have jurisdiction to consider the request for a reduction in such a sentence. Thus, the judge correctly held that the Panel lacked the statutory authority to reduce the 10-year sentence. In the context of the criminal case, however, § 17-10- 6(d) foreclosed the judge's exercise of subject matter jurisdiction over the issue of the underlying constitutionality of the statute. Therefore, the trial court correctly granted a writ of prohibition as to that portion of the judge's order holding § 17-10-6 unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

344 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Rogers v. State


S02A1310.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 67; 575 S.E.2d 879; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 10; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 167



January 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Rogers v. State, 2007 Ga. LEXIS 838 (Ga., Nov. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Right to waive trial on issue of mental retardation; constitutional question. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Walther.
Rogers v. State, 256 Ga. 139, 344 S.E.2d 644, 1986 Ga. LEXIS 725 (1986)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his conviction of murder and his death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal, petitioner initiated state habeas corpus proceedings involving respondent State, seeking a jury trial on the issue of mental retardation. A habeas court found that a genuine issue of fact existed regarding mental retardation, but, after petitioner asked for dismissal, the trial court (Georgia) found a waiver of the right to such a trial. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before the jury trial on petitioner's mental retardation, petitioner wrote a letter to the trial court asking for dismissal of the proceeding. The trial court held a hearing during which petitioner stated that he was not mentally retarded. The trial court found that petitioner knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to a jury trial on the issue. The next month, with new counsel, petitioner sought to set aside the dismissal and withdraw his waiver. Before the court ruled on the motion, however, petitioner again wrote a letter asking for dismissal of the mental retardation trial. The trial court again found a waiver of the right to a trial on mental retardation. The appellate court held that, as petitioner's trial for a capital crime was prior to July 1, 1988, once the habeas corpus court found a genuine issue regarding his mental retardation, the issue had to be thoroughly reviewed and passed upon and was no longer subject to waiver. Contrary to the State's contention, the trial court was not authorized to resolve the matter by finding that petitioner was not mentally retarded; the issue had to be decided by a jury using the definition of retardation in O.C.G.A. § 17-7-131.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings, including a jury trial on the issue of mental retardation.

 

345 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Barnhill v. State


S02A1747.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 155; 575 S.E.2d 460; 2003 Ga. LEXIS 16; 2003 Fulton County D. Rep. 131



January 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 40-5-25 (d); constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Goger.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court denied plaintiff driver's license applicant's request for a declaration that O.C.G.A. § 40-5-25(d), providing that applicants for a Class C driver's license pay a reduced fee if they desired to be organ donors, was unconstitutional on the grounds that it violated substantive due process and equal protection principles. The driver's license applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license applicant sought a Class C driver's license. Because he declined to identify himself as an organ donor, he paid the standard license fee. Thereafter, he brought suit and sought a declaration that O.C.G.A. § 40-5-25(d), providing that applicants for a Class C license pay a reduced fee if they desired to be organ donors, was unconstitutional, because it allegedly violated substantive due process and equal protection principles. The trial court upheld the statute. After that ruling was entered, the state supreme court agreed with the trial court and found that the statute violated neither substantive due process nor equal protection principles. In regard to substantive due process, the state supreme court noted that the statute did not impact on a fundamental right, especially as the right to privacy was not implicated. Accordingly, the state supreme court found the statute was not required to pass a strict scrutiny case in order to be constitutional. The state supreme court also found that, as organ donors were not members of a suspect class, the statute for equal protection purposes only had to pass a rational basis test, which it did.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

346 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Boyd v. State


S02A1081.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 772; 573 S.E.2d 52; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 1061; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 3576



November 25, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Fulton County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Bensonetta Tipton Lane. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-20-01. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-14-01. Lower Ct#: 00SC08298.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of felony murder, with the predicate felony being defendant's possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a convicted felon, got into an argument with a man who was part owner of a tire store. Defendant left, returned to the store with a pistol, and began to argue some more. Defendant then struck the man and fired shots at him. The man was struck once and fatally injured. Evidence indicated that defendant stood above the man and fired the gun downward. Defendant was indicted on multiple criminal charges. At trial, the jury asked the trial court what to do about counts on which they were not unanimous. Also, the trial court found the jury had not considered the lesser-included offense of voluntary manslaughter. The trial court had the jury reconsider all counts of the indictment. The jury found defendant guilty of felony murder, with the predicate offense being possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. After judgment was entered, the state supreme court found that the trial court used the proper procedure in having the jury reconsider all counts and was not required to first void the verdicts. It also found Apprendi did not apply, defendant's trial counsel did not render ineffective assistance, and the evidence was legally sufficient to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

347 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Adams v. State


S02A0974


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 867; 572 S.E.2d 545; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 1024; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 3335



November 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Clayton, County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. William H. Ison. Date of Judgment Appealed: 12-21-01. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-17-02. Lower Ct#: 98CR014522.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Clayton County Superior Court, Georgia, which convicted defendant of malice murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who beat the victim severely with a rock around the head and face, argued, inter alia, that the malice murder statute was unconstitutional because it failed to give notice that the offense can be committed by assaulting a person with a large rock. The instant court concluded that because defendant failed to raise this issue in a timely manner, it was waived. Defendant's remaining enumerations of error had no merit. There was ample evidence showing that defendant was competent to stand trial. Error in preventing a licensed clinical social worker from testifying as an expert regarding opinions formed during her evaluation of defendant was harmless. The social worker was prepared to testify that she made a provisional diagnosis of paranoid-type schizophrenia. The instant court noted that the expert's testimony would have been cumulative of a psychiatrist called by defendant. Regarding defendant's contention that it was error to compel a defense expert to produce a written report for the State, the instant court found no reversible error. The failure to preserve a panel board on which the victim was found did not constitute a denial of due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

348 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Braley v. State


S02P1191.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 47; 572 S.E.2d 583; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 1026; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 3353



November 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 13, 2002.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Braley v. Ga., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6236 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Pike, County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Johnnie Caldwell, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-15-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-12-02. Lower Ct#: 98R147.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Pike County Superior Court (Georgia) of malice murder, felony murder, kidnapping with bodily injury, armed robbery, and aggravated battery. The trial court treated the felony murder verdict as vacated by operation of law, imposed a death sentence for the murder, consecutive terms of life imprisonment for the kidnapping and armed robbery, and 20 years for the aggravated battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed the victim of her bank cards, cut her throat, stabbed her repeatedly, pursued her as she fled, held her until she weakened, and then dragged her away while she was still alive. He was caught while trying to obtain cash from an automated teller machine. The murder weapons were recovered from his car, and he confessed. The supreme court held the evidence was sufficient to convict. As his conviction on the aggravated battery count, which alleged he cut the victim's throat, merged with his malice murder conviction, the former conviction was vacated. All other claimed errors were either not error, had not been preserved, or were harmless. O.C.G.A. §§ 16-5-40 and 16-8-41 (kidnapping and armed robbery) were not unconstitutionally vague. The kidnapping count of the indictment placed defendant on sufficient notice of the charges against him. The State's asking jurors to imagine themselves in the victim's place was error, but was unlikely to have affected the verdict. The evidence sufficed to establish the statutory aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. The death sentence was neither excessive nor disproportionate to the penalties imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence for aggravated battery were vacated, and the other convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

349 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Cross v. Stokes


S02A1067


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 872; 572 S.E.2d 538; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 1030; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 3319



November 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 13, 2002.
Subsequent appeal at, Request denied by, Sub nomine at In re Estate of Robertson, 2005 Ga. App. LEXIS 175 (Ga. Ct. App., Feb. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Estate administration; constitutional question. Fulton County Probate Court. Trial Judge: Honorable Floyd E. Propst. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-16-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-12-02. Lower Ct # :047508.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Veteran Affairs guardian petitioned the Fulton County Probate Court (Georgia) for a declaratory judgment that O.C.G.A. § 29-6-11(c), which prohibited the guardian from being a beneficiary under his ward's will, was unconstitutional. The trial court found the statute constitutional, and the guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Veteran Affairs (DVA) required a guardian for the ward to receive DVA benefits. The supreme court held the guardian timely appealed as he did not have to appeal the implicit disqualification of his taking of the ward's bequest, which was beyond the trial court's jurisdiction in a proceeding to probate the will. The probate court could issue a declaratory judgment. The guardian was clearly a DVA guardian. The probate court's erroneous letters of "general" guardianship instead of DVA guardianship were corrected, and the guardian was appointed under the procedures for appointment of a DVA guardian. O.C.G.A. § 29-6-11(c), preventing the guardian's taking under the ward's will, did not violate Ga. Const. art. III, § V, para. III, prohibiting a bill containing matter different from its title, because it related to the bill's stated purpose of changing DVA guardianships. The statute did not violate the equal protection clauses of the U.S. or Georgia constitutions as it was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in regulating DVA guardianships. The statute was not limited to the guardian's taking, as a beneficiary, of the ward's DVA benefits.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

350 of 777 DOCUMENTS




Terrell v. State


S02P0643.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


276 Ga. 34; 572 S.E.2d 595; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 1025; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 3341



November 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 13, 2002.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Terrell v. Georgia, 540 U.S. 835, 124 S. Ct. 88, 157 L. Ed. 2d 64, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6226 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hall v. Terrell, 285 Ga. 448, 679 S.E.2d 17, 2009 Ga. LEXIS 285 (2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Terrell v. GDCP Warden, 744 F.3d 1255, 2014 U.S. App. LEXIS 4497 (11th Cir. Ga., 2014)
Related proceeding at, Stay denied by Terrell v. Bryson, 2015 U.S. App. LEXIS 21289 (11th Cir. Ga., Dec. 8, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Walton, County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. John M. Ott. Date of Judgment Appealed: 07-23-01. Notice of Appeal Date: 08-09-01. Lower Ct#: 92CR1072, 93CR946-955.
Terrell v. State, 271 Ga. 783, 523 S.E.2d 294, 1999 Ga. LEXIS 909 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, after his third trial, appealed from his conviction in the Walton County Superior Court (Georgia) of malice murder and 10 counts of forgery. The jury recommended, and the trial court imposed, a death sentence for the murder conviction based on three aggravating circumstances. The trial court denied defendant's motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Although the trial court gave the jury an improper charge on using a deadly weapon, this error did not require reversal given the overwhelming evidence of malice. Defendant was permitted to ask sufficient questions on voir dire. Double jeopardy did not bar the death penalty, although a jury had deadlocked in an earlier trial, since the first jury had not adjudicated defendant's sentence or his guilt. The death penalty was not a disproportionate sentence. The State's failure to list the statutory aggravators in the indictment did not violate defendant's constitutional rights. Defendant was put on notice that the State was seeking the death penalty and of the statutory aggravators. The district attorney had the discretion to decide whether defendant met the criteria for the death penalty and whether to pursue it. It was not an abuse of discretion to limit the cross-examination of the State's witness. The transfer of venue was within the trial court's discretion. Georgia's statutory death penalty scheme was constitutional. The appellate court properly reviewed death sentences for proportionality. There were several aggravating factors supporting defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Miller v. State


S02A0626


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 730; 571 S.E.2d 788; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 973; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 3171



October 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 22, 2002.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Miller v. Georgia, 538 U.S. 1004, 123 S. Ct. 1911, 155 L. Ed. 2d 835, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3333 (2003)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Miller v. Martin, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 95679 (N.D. Ga., Feb. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Cherokee, County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. C. Michael Roach. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10/05/00. Notice of Appeal Date: 10/11/00. Lower Ct#: 98CR0722.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cherokee County Superior Court, Georgia, convicted defendant of felony murder, aggravated assault, and aggravated battery and sentenced him to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several claims of error on appeal. The appeals court held that the superior court properly exercised jurisdiction over the case, evidence was sufficient to support the verdicts, the court did not abuse its discretion in ruling on the eligibility of prospective jurors, and there was no prosecutorial misconduct during closing arguments. Specifically, causing brain loss fit the statutory definition of aggravated battery. The jury could find defendant guilty of aggravated assault, as the victim appeared frightened as he exited the bus, was aware that defendant was following him, and had been threatened with physical harm before. Although hands and feet were not deadly weapons per se, the jury could find them to be so depending upon their use. Media coverage did not prevent a fair trial and did not mandate a change of venue. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying motions to strike various jurors for cause. Finally, there were two independent underlying felony convictions that sustained the felony murder conviction. Thus, the felony murder conviction was not deficient for being predicated upon multiple felonies without specification.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Johnson v. State


S02A0712


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 630; 570 S.E.2d 309; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 857; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2820



September 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Lane.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Georgia trial court of malice murder, aggravated assault, and illegal firearm possession. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and three other men entered a barber shop, demanded money, and started fighting with people in the barber shop. One of the other men shot and killed a person when he attempted to flee. Defendant shot and seriously wounded another person who threw a radio at defendant, in an attempt to protect the person's nephew from defendant. At trial, three witnesses identified defendant as one of the assailants and the man who shot the person. Additionally, defendant was listed on the rental agreement of the car used in the robbery, and defendant's cell phone was found in the car. On appeal, the court found that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict; (2) the trial court did not err in sentencing defendant to life in prison for malice murder; (3) the trial court did not err by failing to charge the jury on mutual combat and self defense; (4) the trial court did not err by failing to give a jury charge on voluntary manslaughter, as no evidence was submitted at trial to support such a charge; (5) the trial court's jury charge on malice murder was not burden shifting; and (6) defendant's counsel was not ineffective for not requesting unwarranted jury charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

354 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Noble v. State


S02A1116.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 635; 570 S.E.2d 296; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 858; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2810



September 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391 (a) (5); constitutional question. Atlanta City Court. Before Judge Tharp.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court convicted defendant of driving under the influence (DUI) and another vehicular infraction arising out of two incidents three months apart. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5) was unconstitutionally vague because the term "breath" was not defined therein. The supreme court held that when measured by a "common understanding" of the term "breath," § 40-6-391(a)(5) provided more than adequate notice to a person of ordinary intelligence that driving with an alcohol concentration in excess of 0.08 grams, as measured by grams of alcohol per liters of breath, was criminal conduct. Additionally, there was no error in the State's joinder of the two DUI incidents in one accusation, as there was no risk of prejudice to defendant from a joint disposition of the charges. There was no abuse of the trial court's discretion in denying defendant's motion to sever the charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

355 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Earl v. Mills


S02A0631


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 503; 570 S.E.2d 282; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 875; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2806



September 30, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE REHEARING PERIOD. THIS OPINION IS UNCORRECTED AND SUBJECT TO REVISION BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Earl v. Mills, 2004 Ga. LEXIS 525 (Ga., June 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought a declaratory judgment that a de facto "family court" established by appellee judge and others was illegal and unconstitutional. The Georgia trial court dismissed the claims for attorney fees, costs, and punitive damages. The claims for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief were dismissed after the trial court found they failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The resident appealed.


OVERVIEW: The family court was established by a standing order issued pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-1-9.1(b)(2)(D). Since judges were immune from liability in civil actions for acts performed in their judicial capacity, the trial court did not err when it dismissed that portion of the complaint seeking damages from the judge. The supreme court found there was no appellate decision that controlled the resident's contentions that the judge was without constitutional authority to create a family court because a "family court" was not contained in the Georgia Constitution's listing of the courts in which the judicial power of the state was vested exclusively, and that the standing order resulted in the unconstitutional judicial creation and/or modification of courts and judgeships. However, because the judge did not show that there was an absence of law to support the resident's claims, the trial court erred in dismissing the petition for declaratory and injunctive relief for failure to state a claim.


OUTCOME: That portion of the trial court's judgment dismissing the petition for declaratory and injunctive relief was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for consideration of those issues.

Hanson v. State


S02A1079.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 470; 569 S.E.2d 513; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 646; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2669



September 16, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE REHEARING PERIOD. THIS OPINION IS UNCORRECTED AND SUBJECT TO REVISION BY THE COURT.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the trial court (Georgia) that convicted him of possession of alcohol by a person under 21 years of age in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 3-3-23, claiming that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Responding to a call concerning a fight, a police officer found defendant walking down a street and detected an odor of alcohol. In addition, defendant's speech was slurred, his eyes were glazed, and he told the officer that he had been drinking. The state supreme court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 3-3-23 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because it permitted some under-21-year-olds to possess alcohol, while making it a crime for others to possess alcohol. The legislature had made rational distinctions with respect to the possession of alcohol that recognized that young people were more accountable when they were provided with alcohol under supervised settings or conditions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

357 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Cox v. Barber


S02A1818.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 415; 568 S.E.2d 478; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 629; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2444



August 14, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Barber v. Cox, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 646 (U.S. Jan. 13, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Fulton County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. John S. Langford. Date of Judgment Appealed: 08-07-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 08-12-02. Lower Ct # : 2002CV56692.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an expedited appeal, appellant, the Georgia Secretary of State, appealed from an order by the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) ordering her to place appellee, a candidate, on the primary ballot for the district four seat on the Georgia Public Service Commission (PSC), contending that the one-year residency requirement in Ga. Code Ann. § 46-2-1(b) was constitutional as applied to the candidate.


OVERVIEW: The districts had been reapportioned, causing the candidate to fail the residency requirement. Ga. Code Ann. § 46-2-1(b) required a candidate for the PSC to be a resident of the territory within the district for 12 months prior to the general election. The Georgia Constitution did not create an exception to the one-year residency requirement due to reapportionment of the district. The candidate admitted that he was a resident of Jackson County, which was now in district two, one year before the general election, and did not attempt to become a resident of Banks County in district four until 10 months before the general election. The residency requirement for the PSC was rationally related to the state's legitimate interests in fostering informed voters and promoting knowledgeable and responsive candidates with ties to the community. The requirement did not place an unreasonable burden on the right of voters to choose a candidate or the right of the candidate to run for public office. Requiring the candidate to reside in the district for 12 months prior to the general election did not deny him equal protection under the United States Constitution or the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

358 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Arevalo v. State


S02P0342


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 392; 567 S.E.2d 303; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 571; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2111



July 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 26, 2002.
Reconsideration denied by, 07/26/2002
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Arevalo v. Georgia, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 2761 (U.S., Apr. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Gwinnett County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Fred A. Bishop, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-23-01. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-20-01. Lower Ct#: 98B21096.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Gwinnett County Superior Court (Georgia) of two counts of malice murder, two alternative counts of felony murder, one count of armed robbery, and two counts of possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony. The jury recommended a death sentence for the murders. Defendant's motion for new trial was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplice, with help from defendant's brother, robbed a restaurant. Two workers were fatally shot in the back of the head. Defendant objected to the admission of a letter his brother wrote to him. The appellate court held (1) the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions; (2) jurors whose comments indicated their inability to impose death were properly excluded for cause; (3) no error occurred in not excluding jurors who supported the death penalty; (4) qualifying jurors based on their views on the death penalty views was constitutional; (5) the letter, written in Spanish to "my brother," which discussed in detail crimes defendant and his Spanish-speaking brother were charged with, was properly admitted since it was duly authenticated by circumstantial evidence, the co-conspiracy hearsay exception applied (the conspiracy to conceal the murders having still existed when it was written), and there were sufficient indicia of its reliability; (6) closing argument was proper; (7) victim-impact evidence, the Unified Appeal Procedure, and the death penalty statutes were constitutional; (8) the death sentences were properly imposed, and not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

359 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Young v. State


S02A0224.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 309; 565 S.E.2d 814; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 537; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 2006



July 3, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Implied consent warning, constitutional question. DeKalb County State. Before Trial Judge: Honorable Jack B. Smith. Date of Judgment Appeal: 07-13-01. Notice of Appeal Date: 08-10-01. Lower Ct # 00C093413.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DeKalb County State Court (Georgia) denied defendant's motions to suppress and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of driving while under the influence of alcohol and failure to obey a stop sign. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An arresting officer observed defendant drive through a stop sign and stopped him. His breath smelled of alcohol. The officer asked him to get out of the car. Defendant staggered and performed poorly on field tests. The officer read him a statutory implied consent warning and requested he take breath tests. Defendant's tests showed alcohol concentrations over the legal limit. Defendant moved to suppress the results. He alleged the implied consent warning in Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1 violated the state and federal constitutions' Equal Protection Clause. He argued boaters and hunters, under other statutes, were informed their test results could be used against them at trial, but Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1 did not so advise a motorist. He also contended the breathalyzer machine was not operating properly and the evidence was insufficient. After the motions were denied and he was convicted, the state supreme court found the implied consent warning statute was constitutional since defendant was not similarly situated to boaters and hunters. It also found the State proved both the breathalyzer machine worked properly and he had a sufficient alcohol concentration to be convicted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

360 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Old S. Amusements


S02A0791. S02A0792.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 274; 564 S.E.2d 710; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 449; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 1497



May 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Video Poker Act; constitutional question. Fulton, County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. John J. Goger. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-14-02. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-14-02. Lower Ct#:2001CV46705.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) found in favor of plaintiffs, owners of thousands of video amusement machines, and struck down as unconstitutional the Video Poker Act, which amended Ga. Code Ann. §§ 16-12-20, 16-12-35, and 48-17-1. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the Video Poker Act violated due process because it was so vague and indefinite that men of common intelligence necessarily had to guess at its meaning. The court of appeals disagreed. The Act was sufficiently definite to put those of common intelligence on notice as to what kinds of amusement machines were prohibited, and to restrict any excessive discretion that enforcement authorities could otherwise possess. Applying the rational basis test, the Act bore a rational relation to the State's objective, insuring that amusement machines were not used for illegal cash payouts. Furthermore, the new law did not take business property for a public use; it merely required an already regulated business to adjust its property to the new law.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed.

 

361 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Wells v. City of Baldwin


S02A0356.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 228; 565 S.E.2d 439; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 380; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 1400



May 13, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Taxation; constitutional question. Habersham Superior Court. Before Judge Woods.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners, confronted with an ad valorem property tax liability for the first time in nearly two decades, filed suit challenging appellee city's ordinance. The trial court (Georgia), construing Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-91, upheld the constitutionality of the city's ordinance. The homeowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-91, the city's ordinance was unconstitutional. The city's ordinance violated the Joint County and Municipal Sales and Use Tax Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-66 et seq., by authorizing the city to use the city's pro rata share of revenue generated by a county's local option sales tax (LOST) to roll back the millage rate for the city's county residents. The plain language of the act limited the application of the rollback provision in Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-91 to those residents of the special district where the tax was imposed. Under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-91(a), the city had to uniformly compute the millage rate applicable to all residents necessary to produce revenue sufficient to defray its annual expenses. Only after this calculation was complete could the city assess the impact of LOST revenue it received from a county on its millage rate and reduce that rate to reflect the revenue it obtained from the county. The trial court erred by upholding the validity of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

362 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Payne v. State


S02A0033.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 181; 563 S.E.2d 844; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 388; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 1407



May 13, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 40-6-50 (b); constitutional question. Forsyth Superior Court. Before Judge Mills from Blue Ridge Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of driving in an emergency lane in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-50(b), as well as vehicular homicide, serious injury by vehicle, and reckless driving. He appealed from the court of appeals (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that because "emergency lane" had a meaning commonly understood by drivers following the rules of the road in Georgia, the term, as used in Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-50(b), was sufficiently definite to meet constitutional standards. The court of appeals had repeatedly described the emergency lane as that portion of the paved highway separated from the roadway by solid white lines marking the roadway's borders. Vehicles were permitted to travel on the roadways and not on the paved shoulders, emergency lanes, or within other paved areas divided from the roadways, except in particular instances such as when an emergency existed. Jury instructions were not in error, or any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

363 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Kachwalla


S01A1405.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 886; 561 S.E.2d 403; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 238; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 902



March 25, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391 (a) (2); constitutional question. Gwinnett State Court. Before Judge Hamil.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court granted defendant's demurrer in which he contended that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(2) was an unconstitutional violation of the Equal Protection Clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence of drugs to the extent he was a less safe driver, Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(2). The State argued that the statute was constitutional. The appellate court found that a § 40-6-391(a)(2) violation of the statute, unlike a Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(6) violation, was not a per se violation since impaired driving ability was an element of the crime that had to be proven to obtain a conviction. One accused of violating (a)(2) did not suffer disparate treatment because "less safe to drive" and "rendered incapable of driving safely" were equivalent standards. One was driving under the influence when the ingestion of an intoxicant made one unable to drive as safely as one would have had he/she not ingested. The phrases stated the same proposition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

March 25, 2002, Decided

Writ of certiorari denied Brannan v. Georgia, 537 U.S. 1021, 123 S. Ct. 541, 154 L. Ed. 2d 429, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8373 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hall v. Brannan, 284 Ga. 716, 670 S.E.2d 87, 2008 Ga. LEXIS 871 (2008)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in a Georgia trial court found defendant guilty of malice murder. The jury recommended a death sentence after finding aggravating circumstances. Defendant's motion for new trial was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving his pickup at approximately 98 miles per hour when he was clocked by the deputy sheriff. During pursuit, the deputy activated a video camera in his car. During jury selection, the appellate court found no Batson violation, as the State gave reasons for its strikes, rendering a preliminary showing of prima facie discrimination moot. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motions for mistrial. The prosecutor's arguments were not improper, and if they were, they were corrected by a curative instruction. The appellate court also did not find error in the sentencing phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Raheem v. State


S02P0112.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 87; 560 S.E.2d 680; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 167; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 737



March 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 10, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Raheem v. Georgia, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8372 (U.S. Nov. 12, 2002).

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Henry County Superior Court (Georgia) of malice murder, armed robbery, and burglary, and sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered a friend and the friend's mother. The supreme court found defendant's challenge to the indictment for his vacated felony murder conviction was moot, but the indictment sufficiently pled the statute. 366 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Young v. Williams


S01G0589.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 845; 560 S.E.2d 690; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 201; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 735



March 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended April 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 247 Ga. App. 337.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Dougherty County Superior Court, Georgia, granted appellant doctor's motion for summary judgment regarding appellant patient's medical malpractice action against the doctor, on the ground that the two-year statute of limitation applicable barred the action. The Georgia Court of Appeals adopted the continuous treatment doctrine and reversed the trial court's judgment. The doctor sought a writ of certiorari which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The patient alleged that the doctor failed to diagnose dislocated bones in her left foot. The appellate court reversed the trial court's order on the ground that there was question of fact as to whether the doctor had treated the patient in the two years preceding the filing of her lawsuit. The main issue before the supreme court was whether the appellate court correctly adopted the doctrine of continuous treatment in medical malpractice cases involving misdiagnosis, thus deeming the negligent act to continue as long as the patient remains under the physician's care for the particular disease or condition, for purposes of the applicable statute of limitation. The supreme court held that the legislatively-prescribed statute of limitation did not provide for the commencement of the period of limitation upon the termination of the health-care provider's treatment of the patient, and the judicial branch was not empowered to engraft such a provision on to what the legislature had enacted. Thus, the appellate court's adoption of the continuous treatment doctrine was an error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

367 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Garden Club of Ga. v. Shackelford


S01A0771


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 653; 560 S.E.2d 522; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 93; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 586



February 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 11, 2002. Reconsideration Denied March 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Equity. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette. Garden Club v. Shackelford, 2001 Ga. LEXIS 908, 1 Fulton County D. Rep. 3594 (Ga. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fulton Superior Court, Georgia, upheld Ga. Code Ann. §§ 32-6-75.2 to 32-6-75.3, regarding trimming public foliage around private outdoor advertising, and related administrative rules. Appellant environmental organization sought review. A motion for rehearing was granted, and this opinion was substituted for the court's prior opinion.


OVERVIEW: The legislature adopted a statutory scheme permitting owners of outdoor advertising to trim vegetation on public property blocking the viewing of their advertising. The supreme court held this scheme, Ga. Code Ann. §§ 32-6-75.1 to 75.3, did not violate Ga. Const. art. III, § 6, para. 6, prohibiting legislative donations. The legislature declared that outdoor advertising benefited the state. The statutory provisions required private individuals who benefited financially from the removal of trees on public property to pay for the privilege of enabling the public to view their signs unimpeded by trees and other natural obstructions. This did not amount to an illegal legislative gift. Ga. Code Ann. § 32-6-75.1 required the review of standards and policies regarding trimming and removing vegetation on state rights-of-way by the Roadside Enhancement and Beautification Council, prior to their enactment, and regulations promulgated by the Department of Transportation without awaiting the appointment of that council were invalid for failing to comply with this statutory mandate.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment upholding the contested regulations was reversed, but its judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Lance v. State


S01P1813.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


275 Ga. 11; 560 S.E.2d 663; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 92; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 595



February 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 28, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Lance v. Georgia, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8763 (U.S. Dec. 2, 2002).
Reconsideration denied by, 03/28/2002
Writ of certiorari denied Lance v. Georgia, 537 U.S. 1050, 123 S. Ct. 620, 154 L. Ed. 2d 525, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8763 (Dec. 2, 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hall v. Lance, 286 Ga. 365, 687 S.E.2d 809, 2010 Ga. LEXIS 69 (Jan. 25, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lance v. Warden, Ga. Diagnostic Prison, 2017 U.S. App. LEXIS 16778 (11th Cir. Ga., Aug. 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Jackson Superior Court. Before Judge Motes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Jackson County, Georgia, trial court of murdering two victims and of burglary and possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime. He received, inter alia, two death sentences; he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered his wife and her boyfriend. The supreme court held the evidence was sufficient, and, thus, the death penalty was not precluded. Defendant's conclusory expert witness funds request was correctly denied. Potential jurors were properly not excused for death penalty views, as they could follow the law. A prospective juror who could not impose the death penalty was correctly excused. As defendant did not raise a justification defense, evidence of the victims' characters was properly excluded. Evidence of the victims' drug use was too speculative to show another person's guilt. Prior problems between defendant and the victims were properly admitted. Probable cause existed for issuing search warrants. Defendant's "continuing witness" objection could not apply to demonstrative evidence. It was no error for the trial court to ask witnesses questions from jurors. The jury's aggravating circumstance finding, that one victim's murder was committed during the other victim's murder, was set aside due to the rule against mutually supporting aggravating circumstances. Victim impact testimony was properly received. Defendant's death sentences were proportional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

City of Bremen v. Regions Bank


S01A1732.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 733; 559 S.E.2d 440; 2002 Ga. LEXIS 50; 2002 Fulton County D. Rep. 343



February 4, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal temporary loan; constitutional question. Haralson County Superior. Before Senior Judge: Hon. John S. Langford. Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-20-01. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-12-01. Lower Ct. # : 00433.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the Haralson County Superior Court (Georgia) that granted summary judgment in favor appellee bank, holding the city liable for the payment of a $ 1 million loan issued by the bank, plus interest, penalties, and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the loan was a valid exercise of the city's temporary borrowing power under the Georgia Constitution, and that the tax anticipation note executed as security for the loan was valid on its face and an enforceable obligation. The appellate court also concluded that the bank satisfied its due diligence obligations in connection with the loan. None of the enumerated limitations on the constitutional authority of a municipality to engage in temporary borrowing precluded the city from executing the tax anticipation note as security for the loan from the bank. Based upon the city's representations, the short-term loan from the bank was a valid exercise of the city's temporary borrowing powers. Prior to making the loan, the bank required the city to certify that all of the legal requirements for a temporary loan were satisfied. Moreover, the city certified to the bank that the money borrowed would be used for proper purposes. Having obtained those certifications, and not being in possession of suspicious knowledge that contradicted the city's representations, the bank did not violate its duty of due diligence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Outdoor Sys. v. Cobb County


S01A0859.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 606; 555 S.E.2d 689; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 899; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3487



November 19, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied December 14, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning, etc. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Flournoy. Appellant's motion for reconsideration is granted, the opinion issued by this Court on October 1, 2001, is vacated, and the attached opinion is substituted therefor. There being a substantive change in the opinion, motions for reconsideration may be filed within ten days from the date of this order. Outdoor Sys., Inc. v. Cobb County, 2001 Ga. LEXIS 756, 1 Fulton County D. Rep. 2944 (Ga. 2001) 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant outdoor advertiser restored a nonconforming sign damaged by a tornado and appellee county revoked its permit pursuant to the county's sign ordinance. The advertiser appealed to the board of zoning appeals, which affirmed. A Georgia superior county granted summary judgment in favor of the county as to all claims, and the advertiser appealed. The supreme court granted the advertiser's motion for reconsideration of its earlier opinion.


OVERVIEW: The advertiser contended that summary judgment was erroneous because the sign ordinance conflicted with Ga. Code Ann. § 32-6-83 and was, therefore, void and unenforceable under Ga. Const. art. III, § VI, par. IV(a). The sign ordinance made no provision for compensating the owners of off-premises signs whose permits were revoked. The county urged that the supreme court could not address the constitutionality of its ordinance because the advertiser failed to raise that question before the zoning board. The board could not adjudicate a constitutional claim, and could only act legislatively, so the advertiser met the applicable non-judicial standard in announcing a challenge to the constitutionality on numerous occasions. The county effectuated a removal of the sign without paying the compensation mandated by state law. Under the circumstances, application of the ordinance violated the state constitution. The county could not rely upon an admittedly unconstitutional ordinance in defense of its appeal. The county had no vested right in enforcement of its ordinances which conflicted with Ga. Code Ann. § 32-6-83 and which was, therefore, unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the county was reversed.

Pimper v. State ex rel. Simpson

DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee state obtained an order appointing a receiver and a temporary restraining order (TRO) from the Floyd County Superior Court, Georgia, pursuant to the allegations that appellant officers and their wholly owned corporations violated the Georgia Securities Act, Ga. OVERVIEW: The officer and the corporations were alleged to have been involved in theft, wire fraud, and mail fraud. The officers and the corporations failed to submit evidence in support of their motion to dissolve the TRO and the receivership. The supreme court held that the bankrupt corporations' appeal rested within the exclusive jurisdiction of the bankruptcy court and was subject to the mandatory automatic stay provisions of 11 U.S.C.S. § 362. Code Ann. § 16-14-1 et seq., had been dismissed more than six months prior to the appeal. OUTCOME: The supreme court dismissed the officers' appeal.

Lucas v. State


S01P1069.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 640; 555 S.E.2d 440; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 906; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3495



November 19, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 14, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Lucas v. Georgia, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6265 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Reconsideration denied by, 12/14/2001
Writ of certiorari denied Lucas v. Georgia, 537 U.S. 840, 123 S. Ct. 163, 154 L. Ed. 2d 62, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6265 (2002)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay denied by Lucas v. Upton, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 96015 (M.D. Ga., Oct. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Jones Superior Court. Before Judge Prior.
Rhode v. State, 274 Ga. 377, 552 S.E.2d 855, 2001 Ga. LEXIS 760 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for a Jones County, Georgia, trial court convicted defendant of three counts of malice murder, three counts of felony murder, two counts of burglary, and one count of kidnapping with bodily injury. The felony murder convictions were vacated by operation of law. The jury fixed the sentence for each of the murders at death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was sufficient to find defendant was guilty on all charges. Defendant contended that certain comments during the State's opening statement and certain testimony during the guilt/innocence phase of the trial improperly raised the worth of the victims and the impact wrought by their deaths. OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.


 

373 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Mark Turner Props. v. Evans


S01A1051.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 547; 554 S.E.2d 492; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 860; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3324



November 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied December 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Title to land. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Robinson.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant successor in title filed suit in a Georgia trial court seeking to redeem property sold at a tax sale. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee tax deed holder and the successor in title appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tax sale took place in 1995. The successor in title received quitclaim deeds from the record title holders in 1996 and brought an unsuccessful suit to cancel the tax deed that same year. The successor in title brought the instant suit in 1999 and paid into the trial court registry what it contended was the amount payable for redemption. The trial court found that the 1996 action did not bar the 1999 suit and that the tax deed holder had waived the requirement of tender by refusing to communicate with the successor in title. However, the trial court also found that the amount paid into the trial court registry was insufficient and that the title conveyed by the tax deed had ripened by prescription. The appellate court found that the tax deed holder did not have prescriptive title, as she had done nothing more than pay taxes on the property. The trial court correctly determined that the tax deed holder waived tender and that the amount paid into the registry was insufficient for redemption. However, insufficiency of payment did not prevent the successor in title from redeeming the property where it stood ready, willing, and able to pay the redemption price.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed to the extent that the trial court found that the suit was not barred and that tender had been waived, but the judgment was reversed to the extent that the trial court held that the successor in title was not allowed to redeem the property. The case was remanded.

In re C.P.


S01A0748.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 599; 555 S.E.2d 426; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 867; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3327



November 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 14, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Delinquency. Rockdale Juvenile Court. Before Judge Schneider.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition alleging defendant juvenile was a delinquent and unruly child because she was unmarried and engaged in an act of sexual intercourse in a stall in a restroom in a high school. The juvenile unsuccessfully sought to quash the petition. Thereafter, she filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the juvenile argued the delinquency petition failed to set out a specific violation of Georgia law in that the fornication statute underlying the petition was an unconstitutional violation of a citizen's liberty of privacy. She further asserted that it was unconstitutional to use as the offense underlying a petition for delinquency an act that would be protected activity if committed by an adult. The appellate court initially noted the right of privacy was not absolute since its successful exercise was dependent upon the facts and circumstances from which its assertion arose. The appellate court held the right of privacy did not protect all sexual conduct from prosecution. The appellate court concluded because the right of privacy was dependent upon the facts of each case, to the point they had been developed, the juvenile's case neither supported the successful assertion of the right to privacy nor served as the basis for quashing the petition alleging delinquency and unruliness on her part.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

375 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Massaline v. Williams


S01A1182.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 552; 554 S.E.2d 720; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 827; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3171



October 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Reconsideration denied December 3, 2001. Habeas corpus. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Conner.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Gwinett County Superior Court, Georgia, denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was incarcerated and without representation. He filed a pro se application for a certificate of probable cause to appeal, which was dismissed as untimely. The supreme court granted his motion to reconsider. The court adopted a mailbox rule under which a pro se prisoner's application should be deemed filed on the date he delivered it to the prison authorities for forwarding to the clerk of court. Unlike litigants who were not incarcerated, pro se prisoners could not monitor the processing of their appellate filings to ensure that the clerk of the court timely received them. They could not personally travel to the courthouse to see that their filings were filed timely, and could not regularly call the clerk of court to monitor whether their filings were received. Of course, being pro se, they could not rely on their lawyer to ensure the safe and timely filing of their appeals. Pro se prisoners also had to entrust their legal papers to the prison officials. No matter how far in advance the pro se prisoner delivered his notice to the prison authorities, he could never be sure that it would ultimately get stamped filed on time.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

376 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Pecina v. State


S01A1186.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 416; 554 S.E.2d 167; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 830; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3160



October 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 40-6-394; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Manis.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before a Georgia trial court, of driving under the influence of alcohol to the extent that it was less safe for him to drive than if he was not so influenced, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(1), and serious injury by vehicle, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-394. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving a pickup truck that collided with an automobile. The other driver's mother was seated in the front passenger seat of the automobile. Injuries to the driver's mother were the basis of the charge of serious injury by vehicle. On appeal, defendant contended that the serious injury by vehicle statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-394, was unconstitutional as applied to him. Under the facts of the case, the proscription against seriously disfiguring a bodily member was not applied in an unconstitutional manner. The driver's mother suffered two broken legs just above the knees; both were shattered into dozens of pieces. Given the nature of the driver's mother's injuries, the prohibition against causing bodily harm to another by seriously disfiguring his body gave defendant due notice that it prohibited the acts for which he has been convicted. Despite defendant's argument to the contrary, the evidence was sufficient to sustain a conviction. The trial court did not err by admitting into evidence other similar acts, nor were the jury instructions erroneous.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Dawson v. State


S01A1041., S01A1210.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 327; 554 S.E.2d 137; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 785; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2950



October 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Dawson v. State, 2008 Ga. LEXIS 257 (Ga., Mar. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Case No. S01A1041 Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shoob. (S01A1041) Fulton County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Wendy Lee Shoob. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-27-01. Lower Court#: Y11554.

(S01A1210) Monroe County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Arthur Fudger. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-29-01. Lower Ct#: 8676.
Moore v. State, 240 Ga. 807, 243 S.E.2d 1, 1978 Ga. LEXIS 839 (1978)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S01A1041. Judgment reversed in Case No. S01A1210.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), held that defendant, sentenced to death for four murders, could not be executed by electrocution as this method of execution was unconstitutional. The Monroe County Superior Court (Georgia), where a second defendant had been sentenced to death for murder and rape, held that his execution by electrocution was constitutional. The cases were consolidated for review.


OVERVIEW: The lower court which held that execution by electrocution was constitutional received evidence from state and defense experts, autopsy reports, statements of electrocution survivors, and post-mortem photos of executed persons. In the other lower court, only defendant put on such evidence, some of which was objected to by the State. As this evidence was cumulative, the instant court considered only evidence received by the first court. This evidence showed that two or more applications of current were sometimes needed to kill the prisoner, electrocution could cause pain and horror, electrocution burned and blistered the body, and destroyed the brain by cooking it. The instant court held that death by electrocution inflicted purposeless physical violence and needless mutilation, and violated the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment of Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. XV. The legislature's adoption of lethal injection provided a less painful, less barbarous means of execution. Death sentences that formerly would have been executed by electrocution were not void, but future executions were to be carried out by lethal injection under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-38.


OUTCOME: The judgment that upheld the constitutionality of execution by electrocution was reversed. The judgment that held execution by electrocution to be unconstitutional was affirmed.

 

378 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Adams v. Ga. Dep't of Corr.


S01A1295.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 461; 553 S.E.2d 798; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 794; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 3001



October 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court granted appellees', Georgia Department of Corrections, commissioner, and Georgia Board of Corrections, motion to dismiss appellants', opponents of capital punishment, mandamus action to prohibit appellees from using the electric chair as Georgia's means of execution. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that, as citizens of Georgia, they had standing to seek enforcement of appellees' duty to obey the constitutional prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The existence of standing under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-6-24 depended upon whether appellees owed a public duty which appellants, as members of the public, were entitled to have enforced. Contrary to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-6-24, appellants sought to prevent, rather than to enforce, the performance of a public duty. Appellants' challenge was to the very constitutionality of the underlying enactment pursuant to which appellees were compelled to perform their obligation of carrying out all lawfully imposed criminal sentences. The Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution and the comparable Georgia constitutional provision were not intended to benefit the public at large. Appellants were not directly adversely affected by the enforcement of the statute, because they were not charged with or convicted of a capital crime. Because appellants raised a political challenge and sought to block the performance of a public duty, the trial court properly dismissed the mandamus petition for lack of standing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

379 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Yates v. State


S01P0977.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 312; 553 S.E.2d 563; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 757; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2947



October 1, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge Miller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Georgia trial court of malice murder, burglary, and aggravated assault, and was sentenced to the death penalty. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered a former girlfriend. At trial, his motion that the trial court personally determine all excusals from jury service and provide defendant notice and an opportunity to be heard was granted. The clerk excused 49 of 160 potential jurors without notice. The trial court was authorized to excuse potential jurors based on a determination that jury service would pose an undue hardship, but the lack of inquiry into proffered medical excuses meant there was no determination of undue hardship and abused discretion; this error affecting the jury array composition required a new trial. The lack of a written order authorizing the clerk to excuse jurors and providing guidelines also abused discretion. The trial court did not have to give a jury instruction on voluntary manslaughter since evidence of a sudden, violent, and irresistible passion resulting from serious provocation was lacking. Forced balancing to ensure the racial balance in a grand or traverse jury pool reflected the racial balance in the county population and was not unconstitutional. The victim's prior statement was not shown to be admissible under the necessity exception to the hearsay rule.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were reversed, and the matter was remanded.

Dye v. Wallace


S01A0625.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 257; 553 S.E.2d 561; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 759; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2928; 29 Media L. Rep. 2534



October 1, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-6-23; constitutional question. McDuffie Superior Court. Before Judge Dunaway.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court granted summary judgment to appellees, reporter and newspaper, in appellant guardian's suit for invasion of privacy by unlawful publication. The guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court declared Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-23, the Rape Confidentiality Statute, to be unconstitutional. The criminal assault on the child was a matter of legitimate public concern, and the reporter and newspaper lawfully obtained the information about the assault from a police report generated during the investigation of the crime and made available to the public. The guardian sought to impose civil liability pursuant to the Rape Confidentiality Statute. However, where a newspaper published truthful information which it lawfully obtained, punishment could only be imposed, if at all, when narrowly tailored to a state interest of the highest order. The State failed to utilize a more limited means of guarding against dissemination of the child's identity, the statute promulgated the self-censorship concerns, it had the same broad negligence per se standard found objectionable, and suffered from the same underinclusiveness as an earlier case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

381 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Pryor Org. v. Stewart


S01A1174.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 487; 554 S.E.2d 132; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 769; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2934



October 1, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied November 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Spalding Superior Court. Before Judge English.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bondsman sought mandamus in the Georgia trial court to require appellee sheriff to allow it to continue to write bonds in the sheriff's county. The trial court denied the petition, and the bondsman appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff did not let the bondsman write bail bonds in the county, giving no reasons, but later raising the bondsman's arrest for impersonating a police officer, a charge later dropped, and the bondsman filming a commercial at the jail, stating this violated Ga. Code Ann. § 17-6-52, prohibiting a bondsman from soliciting business at a jail. Section 17-6-52, a criminal statute, had to be strictly construed in the bondsman's favor, and did not apply to a solicitation of the general public filmed at a jail, since the bondsman's presence there was not to solicit potential clients currently incarcerated, so the commercial did not support the sheriff's decision. The bondsman's arrest, even though charges were later dropped, allowed the sheriff to find the bondsman was not of "good moral character," under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-6-50(3), and was a valid basis for his decision. The phrase "good moral character" was not unconstitutionally vague, and the argument was not raised in the trial court. The sheriff's initial failure to specify a reason for his actions did not violate due process, since it was cured by a subsequent specification. That argument was also not raised in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed, for different reasons.

City of Atlanta v. S.W.A.N. Consulting & Sec. Servs.


S01A0952.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 277; 553 S.E.2d 594; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 782; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2931



October 1, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] City ordinance; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Carnes, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Georgia trial court granted appellee security company's petition for injunctive and declaratory relief, wherein it argued Atlanta, Ga., Code § 10-206(a) (1999) was unconstitutional as applied to it. Appellant city challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The city had amended its municipal code to provide that private companies providing security services at an adult entertainment establishment were required to have a city-issued permit of eligibility to provide those services and to register with the board of private detective and security agencies. The security company successfully challenged the ordinance, arguing by expressly authorizing additional local regulation of the security business, the Georgia Private Detective and Security Agencies Act impliedly preempted the city's regulation of those services in its adult entertainment establishments. The appellate court held under Ga. Const. art. III, § 4(a) (1983), no special law could be enacted in any case for which provision had been made by an existing general law. The appellate court concluded because the city sought to establish a duplicate regulatory system which was not authorized by the comprehensive general law applicable to those engaged in the private security business, the trial court was correct that the general act preempted by implication the city's enforcement of Atlanta, Ga., Code § 10-206(a) (1999) against the security company.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Rhode v. State


S01P0708.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 377; 552 S.E.2d 855; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 760; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2957



October 1, 2001, Decided

Writ of certiorari denied Rhode v. Georgia, 536 U.S. 925, 122 S. Ct. 2593, 153 L. Ed. 2d 782, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4512 (2002)
Rehearing denied by Rhode v. Georgia, 536 U.S. 983, 123 S. Ct. 19, 153 L. Ed. 2d 883, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5308 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Rhode v. Hall, 582 F.3d 1273, 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 20712 (11th Cir. Ga., 2009)

PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Jones Superior Court. Before Judge Wingfield.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Georgia trial court found defendant guilty of three counts each of malice and felony murder, two counts of burglary, and one count of kidnapping with bodily injury. The felony murder convictions were vacated. The jury found the depravity aggravator and that the murders were committed in the commission of each other or the other crimes. The murder sentences were death, with life for kidnapping and 20 years for burglary. He appealed.

Defendant and the co-perpetrator subdued him, the co-perpetrator non-fatally wounded the boy, defendant seated and shot twice a female resident who arrived, and the co-perpetrator repeatedly shot the boy.
