The Georgia Supreme Court held that the trial court did not err by failing to excuse sua sponte 12 contested prospective jurors who were not challenged for cause based on their death penalty views. The rule against mutually-supporting aggravators was not violated. Admission of juvenile confessions of defendant at sentencing was not error. Defendant's attack of a jail guard while awaiting trial was relevant in proportionality review, as was his co-defendant's death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.


 

384 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Bagby v. State


S01A1056.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 222; 552 S.E.2d 807; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 623



September 17, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-12-1 (b) (3); constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Winegarden.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A grand jury indicted defendant for contributing to the deprivation of a minor, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-1(b)(3). She filed a general demurrer and motion to quash the indictment, asserting that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The motion was denied and the case was tried before a Georgia trial court on a written stipulation of facts. Defendant was found guilty and appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-1(b)(3) was unconstitutionally vague because the definition of "deprived child" contained in Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-2, and incorporated in Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-1(b)(3), failed to give adequate notice of the prohibited conduct. The supreme court disagreed. Measured by common understanding, the statute prohibited a person from willfully committing an act or omission that deprived a child of the physical, mental, emotional, or moral needs essential to the child's well-being. It was of no consequence that the definition of "deprived child," like other provisions of the code relating to juvenile proceedings, had to be liberally construed. Even strictly construed, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-1(b)(3) provided sufficient warning to a person of ordinary intelligence that leaving the three-year-old victim alone with a third party who had previously beaten the child and was under the influence of methamphetamine, and then locking the child in a bathroom instead of promptly seeking medical attention after the third party had inflicted multiple skull fractures on her was prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

At&T Corp. v. Sigala

The corporation moved for dismissal on the basis of forum non conveniens. The Fulton County Trial Court, Georgia, denied the motion and the corporation appealed.

London v. State


S01A0404.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 91; 549 S.E.2d 394; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 585; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2237



July 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder.  [***1] Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Ingram. Trial Judge: Hon. S. Lark Ingram. Lower Ct # 969052234.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cobb County Superior Court, Georgia, convicted defendant of malice murder, two counts of felony murder, and cruelty to children. Defendant appealed the denial of his amended motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions because the evidence was entirely circumstantial. Extensive trial testimony from medical personnel established that the victim had been abused prior to the fall and that the fall itself could cause injuries of such magnitude only if she had been thrown down the stairs. The jury was authorized to conclude it was not the first time the victim had been left in defendant's care and suffered a serious injury. Defendant contended the trial court erred in admitting the testimony of the victim's sister, who was four years old. A child was not incompetent as a matter of law because of her infancy. The sister's statements were admissible as prior inconsistent statements. The sister answered numerous questions regarding herself and the crime. The sister was available for cross-examination, and defendant was free to question her at trial regarding the reasons for her forgetfulness, confusion, and evasion. There was no reasonable possibility that the jury would have returned a different verdict had the trial court not allowed the sister's testimony. Trial counsel was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Roswell v. Outdoor Sys.


S01A0117.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 130; 549 S.E.2d 90; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 537; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 2061



July 2, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied, July 26, 2001


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Westmoreland.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city requested discretionary review to consider the decision of the Fulton County Superior Court, Georgia, that a moratorium on applications for billboard signs was void as the city failed to comply with the notice provisions of Ga. Code Ann. § 36-66-4.


OVERVIEW: The City of Roswell enacted a temporary moratorium on applications for billboard signs after its sign ordinance was struck down as unconstitutional. Appellee billboard company filed four applications to construct billboard signs. When the city failed to approve them, the billboard company filed a petition for mandamus, which the trial court granted. On appeal, the court held that the city's temporary moratorium on billboard sign applications was not a final legislative action, but a brief ban on applications lasting approximately one month. It did not permanently suspend all applications or prohibit them. It was merely enacted as an emergency measure to preserve the status quo for 30 days pending its enactment of a new ordinance. It was a reasonable interim action and therefore exempt from the procedural requirements of Ga. Code Ann. § 36-66-4. Because the city did not have to comply with the statute's notice requirements in briefly suspending its acceptance of applications for large billboard signs, the moratorium was valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Consol. Gov't of Columbus v. Barwick


S01A0564, S01A0565.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 176; 549 S.E.2d 73; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 529; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 1984



June 25, 2001, Decided

DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee restaurant filed a petition for certiorari and a complaint for mandamus, a temporary restraining order, and declaratory relief with the Muscogee County Superior Court (Georgia), after appellant city did not reissue an alcoholic beverage license. The trial court ruled that Columbus, Georgia Ordinance § 3-5(d), was unconstitutional and that Columbus, Georgia Ordinance § 3-1(f), was unconstitutional as applied. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city did not reissue an alcoholic beverage license to the restaurant because the restaurant was located within 600 feet of another location already holding an alcohol license, § 3-5(d), and the restaurant did not meet the criteria for a restaurant, § 3-1(f). The trial court found § 3-5(d) was unconstitutional because similarly situated businesses were exempt from the distance requirement and § 3-1(f) was unconstitutionally applied. On appeal, the supreme court found the issues were properly before the court on applications for discretionary appeal. Further, the distance requirement of § 3-5(d) was constitutional. Finally, the 600-foot exemption for establishments in the area where the restaurant was located bore a rational relationship to a legitimate government concern, and did not constitute a denial of equal protection.


OUTCOME: Judgments were reversed.

In re L.C.


S01A0197.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 886; 548 S.E.2d 335; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 453; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 1861



June 11, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Designated felony statute; constitutional question. Gwinnett Juvenile Court. Before Judge Franzen.  Lower Court: Gwinnett County Juvenile Court. Trial Judge: Hon. Stephen E. Franzen. Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-23-00. Lower Ct. #:00025472.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the judgment of the Gwinnett County Juvenile Court (Georgia) that convicted him of aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: After the juvenile was convicted of assault, the trial court ordered that he be confined to a youth development center for 12 months, and then be placed under intensive supervision for 12 months. The juvenile appealed, claiming that Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-63 violated his constitutional right to a jury trial. The appellate court disagreed, and affirmed. The juvenile had no due process right to a jury trial, since an adjudication of delinquency was not equivalent to conviction of a crime, the primary function of the delinquency laws was treatment and rehabilitation, and adjudication of delinquency did not carry the same civil disabilities as conviction of a crime. That § 15-11-63 provided for longer periods of confinement than the prior statute did not make the treatment of juvenile offenders sufficiently similar to that of adults as to trigger the right to a jury trial. The juvenile raised other constitutional objections to the statute, but as he did not specify either the particular part or parts of the statute that he was challenging or how those part or parts of the statute violated the constitutional provisions, the claims were not reviewed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cobb County v. Crusselle


S01A0474, S01A0476.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


274 Ga. 78; 548 S.E.2d 306; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 419; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 1807



June 4, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration [**1] Denied July 16, 2001. As Amended July 16, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Development standard; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Stoddard.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the decision of the Cobb County Superior Court, Georgia, which held that a portion of Cobb County, Ga., Dev. Stand. 409.01.02 unconstitutionally conflicted with the practice of land surveying as defined in Ga. Code Ann. § 43-15-2(6)(D).


OVERVIEW: On review, the supreme court found that Cobb County, Ga., Dev. Stand. 409.01.02 required storm sewer systems designs within county boundaries be approved by a registered civil engineer while Ga. Code Ann. § 43-15-2(6) set forth certain activities which a professional land surveyor could perform but did not purport to reserve these designated activities for performance exclusively by land surveyors; furthermore, nothing in the statute prohibited the performance of these activities by other qualified professionals who were lawfully authorized to undertake them. Therefore, the requirement in the development standard that sewer systems be approved by a registered civil engineer thus did not detract from or hinder the operation of § 43-15-2(6).


OUTCOME: That part of the trial court's ruling finding the standard to be unconstitutional was reversed; that portion upholding its validity was affirmed.

Youngblood v. Gwinnett Rockdale Newton Cmty. Serv. Bd.


S00A1784.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 715; 545 S.E.2d 875; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 295; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 1743

PRIOR HISTORY: Community service boards, sovereign immunity; constitutional question. Gwinnett State Court. Before Judge Cook.

This Opinion Substituted for Vacated Opinion of March 2, 2001, Previously Reported at: 2001 Ga. LEXIS 209.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, as guardian of her daughter, challenged the order of the Georgia trial court, granting summary judgment in favor of appellee, on her breach of contract and negligence claims which arose when her daughter was in appellee's care.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, on behalf of her daughter who was injured while in appellee's care, brought suit alleging breach of contract and negligence. However, appellant alleged she would possibly be an intended third party beneficiary, and thus have standing to maintain an action. The court agreed, and remanded the case to the trial court for consideration.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, granting summary judgment on appellant's claims was affirmed. However, judgment was reversed on the breach of contract claim, for consideration of appellant's claim as a possible third party beneficiary.

 

393 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Tyson


S00G0606., S00A2019.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 690; 544 S.E.2d 444; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 273; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 1040



March 29, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Case No. S00G0606 Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 241 Ga. App. 288. Case No. S00A2019 Certiorari jurisdiction; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Robinson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S00A2019. Judgment reversed in Case No. S00G0606.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court of appeals of Georgia reversed appellee's conviction of child molestation on the grounds that the trial court erred in not suppressing evidence obtained from an illegal arrest. The State of Georgia sought certiorari, and appellee filed a motion to dismiss the writ as improvidently granted.


OVERVIEW: The officer who arrested appellee knew from three complainants that a man had fondled a child; two complainants had identified appellee as the molester. The officer entered appellee's van with his consent, found used latex gloves, petroleum jelly, female underpants, and loaded guns. In appellee's trial for child molestation, the trial court denied appellee's motion to suppress evidence seized after his arrest, holding that appellee's warrantless arrest was lawful. The court of appeals reversed, finding that the arrest was illegal. The State petitioned for a writ of certiorari. The instant court granted the writ, and reversed. First, it held that it had jurisdiction under the Georgia Constitution to review, at the State's request, court of appeals decisions that favored criminal defendants. Second, it found that the arrest was supported by probable cause and was legal; thus, the trial court did not err in admitting evidence seized from the van. Appellee waived his right to claim error in the admission of sexually explicit material by not objecting at trial. Evidence he did object to was either properly admitted, or its admission was not deemed reversible error.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the court of appeals reversed, and that of the trial court affirmed. The supreme court had the power, derived from the state constitution and independent of statute, to review the State's appeal from the court of appeals' decision in favor of appellee. The trial court correctly concluded that appellee's arrest was supported by probable cause, so its denial of appellee's motion to suppress evidence obtained in the arrest was proper.

 

394 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Wickham v. State


S00A1796.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 563; 544 S.E.2d 439; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 270; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 954



March 21, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] City Court of Atlanta; constitutional question. Fulton County City Court. Trial Judge: Hon. Lenwood A. Jackson. Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-25-00. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-11-00. Lower Ct # :200424.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Georgia granted appellant interlocutory review to address his assertion that the City Court of Atlanta was unconstitutional after the Fulton County City Court (Georgia) denied his constitutional challenge to the existence of the City Court of Atlanta was denied.


OVERVIEW: The City Court of Atlanta, under 1996 Ga. Laws 627, did not violate the exclusivity and uniformity provisions of the 1983 Georgia Constitution, art. VI, § I, paras. I and V. 1983 Ga. Const., art. VI, § I, par. V expressly acknowledges the existence of non-uniform courts, stating that the courts of each class are to have uniform jurisdiction except as otherwise provided in the Georgia Constitution. art., § X, par. I, cites the City Court of Atlanta by name and provides that it, along with other specified courts and administrative agencies having quasi-judicial powers, shall continue with the same jurisdiction as such courts and agencies have on the effective date of this article until otherwise provided by law. The City Court of Atlanta did not lack constitutional existence; therefore, contrary to appellant's contention, its exercise of jurisdiction did not run afoul of state or federal due process.


OUTCOME: The denial of the constitutional challenge was affirmed.

 

395 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Foster v. State


S00A2054.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 555; 544 S.E.2d 153; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 261; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 942



March 19, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Houston County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Carl A. Veline, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-16-00. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-17-00. Lower Ct # :99C59764.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was cited for violating Houston County Animal Control Ordinance § 10-20 in the Houston County Superior Court (Georgia) because he owned more than four dogs and/or cats without a special permit. The trial court found defendant guilty and imposed sentence. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant kept 11 dogs on his property. After defendant was warned that he was in violation of Houston County, Georgia Animal Control Ordinance § 10-20 by keeping more than four dogs and/or cats without a special permit, defendant applied for a special permit. His application was denied with no grounds specified. Defendant kept his dogs and challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance alleging it was vague and ambiguous. The Georgia Supreme Court found the provisions of the ordinance provided defendant with notice he was forbidden to have more than four dogs and/or cats until he obtained a permit. However, the ordinance did not establish a standard by which the permit application would be judged. Therefore, the granting or denying of permits was purely discretionary and was incompatible with due process.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed as ordinance did not establish criteria by which special permits to have more than four dogs and/or cats were to be granted or denied.

 

396 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Peterson


S00A1512.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 657; 543 S.E.2d 692; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 192; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 798



March 2, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied April 6, 2001.
Certiorari Denied October 9, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 9551.
Reconsideration denied by, 04/06/2001
Writ of certiorari denied Peterson v. Georgia, 534 U.S. 955, 122 S. Ct. 356, 151 L. Ed. 2d 269, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 9551 (2001)
Related proceeding at Fulton-DeKalb Hosp. Auth. v. Reliance Trust Co., 270 Ga. App. 822, 608 S.E.2d 272, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 1549 (2004)
Subsequent appeal at Peterson v. State, 282 Ga. 286, 647 S.E.2d 592, 2007 Ga. LEXIS 532 (Ga., July 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion to suppress. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Lane.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were indicted for murder, assault, battery, and child cruelty. The Fulton County Superior Court, Georgia, granted defendants' motion to suppress evidence seized from their home. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A detective assigned to a 911 case went to the hospital and viewed the bruised corpse of a child. After consulting with medical personnel he formed the opinion that the child had been an abuse victim. He learned that two children were still at the home from which 911 had been called. He went there and was let in by two uniformed officers who told him that they were caring for the children. There he saw and seized pantyhose on a banister, notes on a door referring to abuse by tying, and a belt and cord that may have caused the dead child's wounds. Defendants, adult residents, were indicted for murder, assault, battery, and cruelty. Defendants' motion to suppress was granted. The court reversed. The detective could join his colleagues at the home even though the exigency justifying invasion no longer existed. Also, insufficient care by the officers already present could itself have been an exigency. There was no showing that an exigency had been manufactured or that the detective's intrusion expanded the initial police intrusion. The seized items were in plain view.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed. Child abuse detective's intrusion into home already secured by other officers, and subsequent plain view seizure of evidence, was justified because he could constitutionally join his fellow officers, no exigency was manufactured, and he had not expanded the initial police intrusion.

 

397 of 777 DOCUMENTS



Mathis v. State


S00A1760.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 508; 543 S.E.2d 712; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 196; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 791



March 2, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Gwinnett County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. James W. Oxendine. Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-17-00. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-24-00. Lower Ct # :99B018481.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Gwinnett County Superior Court (Georgia) denying his motion for new trial from his convictions for armed robbery, hijacking a motor vehicle, and kidnapping, arguing Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-44.1(d) violated the state constitutional prohibition against double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: The complainant alleged appellant accosted her outside her apartment with a weapon and demanded the keys to her vehicle. Appellant was later arrested and convicted of armed robbery, hijacking a motor vehicle, and kidnapping. He filed a motion for a new trial, asserting multifarious error, including a challenge to the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-44.1 which provided the offense of hijacking a motor vehicle was to be considered a separate offense not to merge with any other offense, and that punishment for the offense was not to be deferred, suspended, or probated. The trial court denied the motion and appellant challenged the ruling. The court held the double jeopardy clause of the Georgia constitution protected against a second prosecution for the same offense after acquittal or conviction, and multiple punishments for the same offense. The court admonished it did not prohibit additional punishment for a separate offense which the general assembly intended a separate sanction. The court went on to affirm, finding appellant's additional arguments unmeritorious.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because while the Georgia double jeopardy clause proscribed a second prosecution for the same offense after acquittal or conviction and multiple punishments for the same offense, it did not prohibit additional punishment for a separate offense which the general assembly deemed worthy of a separate sanction.

 

398 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hartrampf


S00A2081.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 522; 544 S.E.2d 130; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 203; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 807



March 2, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sign ordinance; constitutional question. Cobb State Court. Before Judge Adams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment of the Cobb State Court, Georgia, finding that, as applied in this case, a county sign ordinance effected an unconstitutional taking by preventing the repair of appellees' "grandfathered" non-conforming sign without compensation for the sign.


OVERVIEW: Appellees were charged with 168 criminal violations of a county's sign ordinances. The alleged violations stemmed from a particular ordinance, which regulated the conditions under which existing off-premises advertising signs could be perpetuated. The trial court found that, as applied in this case, the ordinance effected an unconstitutional taking by preventing the repair of a "grandfathered" non-conforming sign without compensation for the sign. The State appealed, contending that Ga. Code Ann. § 32-6-83, the statute requiring compensation, did not apply because appellees did not have a lawful right to use the sign at the time a tornado damaged it because the lot was a non-conforming size and had no means of ingress and egress. Judgment was affirmed. The sign ordinance at issue was inapplicable because it would have operated to do that which § 32-6-83 declared it could not do. The lot size and access problems were a result of the condemnation and were changed conditions beyond the control of the sign owner. Any tornado damage to the sign that resulted in the sign's failure to meet ordinance requirements was also a changed condition beyond the control of the sign owner.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Because appellees' placement of its sign was rendered illegal by the condemnation and consequent failure to comply with a county sign ordinance, the county could not, under a state statute regulating takings, cause it to be removed by operation of the ordinance without compensation. Further, trial court did not err in concluding that the repair of the sign following the tornado did not require a permit.

 

399 of 777 DOCUMENTS



State v. Wooten


S00G1574.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 529; 543 S.E.2d 721; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 210; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 805



March 2, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Dade County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Jon B. Wood. Lower Ct # :A99A2268 97RC10633.

Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 244 Ga. App. 101.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State applied for a writ of certiorari to challenge a Georgia Court of Appeals decision that reversed criminal defendant's conviction entered in the trial court on the grounds that the trial court's system for assigning cases in the trial court violated state law. Defendant had been convicted of four counts of child molestation.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was charged with four counts of child molestation. At trial, the trial court used its normal system for assigning case in which the district attorney called the case for trial and assigned it to a judge. The jury convicted defendant on all four counts. Thereafter, in a separate case, the state supreme court found that the case assignment system violated state law. On appeal, the appellate court reversed defendant's conviction based on the state supreme court's decision that the trial court's case assignment system violated state law. The State applied to the court for a writ of certiorari. The court granted the writ and reversed the appellate court's decision. Due to the district attorney's limited role in assigning cases to a judge and calling the court calendar, defendant's state and federal constitutional rights were not violated. Too, while the trial court erred in using the system, the error in using it was harmless. The district attorney's limited discretion and the subsequent independent roles that the trial judge and jury played made it highly improbable the error contributed to the jury's guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded because the district attorney's limited role in assigning cases to a judge and calling the court calendar--the trial court's system for assigning cases--did not violate defendant's federal or state constitutional rights. Also, it was highly improbable the error in allowing defendant's case to proceed under that system contributed to the verdict finding defendant guilty on all four child molestation counts.

 

400 of 777 DOCUMENTS




Colwell v. State


S00P1959.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


273 Ga. 634; 544 S.E.2d 120; 2001 Ga. LEXIS 201; 2001 Fulton County D. Rep. 780



March 2, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 5, 2001. Certiorari Denied October 15, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 9786.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Sumter Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Sumter County Superior Court, Georgia, contending the court improperly found him competent to stand trial, erred by denying him a right to represent himself, by failing to conduct a hearing on his competence, and by forcing representation upon him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to, inter alia, two counts of malice murder, six counts of felony murder, and two counts of aggravated assault, resulting from his plan to effectuate his own death by capital punishment. He received eight death sentences. On appeal, the court held defendant was properly found competent, the trial judge did not force representation upon him, and did not err in refusing a request to proceed pro se. Defendant's execution was not suicide because the sentence was based on the nature of his crimes, not his own desire to die. Further, the jury made the final determination of death as the appropriate punishment. The court further set aside the six felony murder convictions and death sentences, as similar to malice murder, and the two aggravated assault convictions under the merger doctrine. Finally, the court found the death penalty was not an excessive sentence as to one victim given the outrageous and vile nature of the crime committed, but could not find the statutory aggravated circumstance regarding the aggravated battery to that victim's wife. The same error also appeared in her murder because mutually supporting aggravating circumstances were impermissible.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, vacated in part. Two of the death sentences affirmed, vacated were the six convictions and death sentences for felony murder, the convictions and sentences for aggravated assault. Defendant not coerced into representing himself as he fully understood the nature and extent of the proceedings.
